Definition and Types of 'Arad Dhati in Hanafi Usul
Defining 'arad dhati and its three types in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of 'arad dhati and apply the classification to determine which accidents are investigated in a given science.

Core Idea
Essential accidents stem from the essence of the subject; only these form the proper domain of a science.

This passage introduces a foundational concept in Hanafi usul: the classification of accidents into essential ('arad dhati) and extraneous ('arad gharib). Understanding this distinction is crucial because a science only investigates the essential accidents of its subject, not every attribute. The commentator defines three types of 'arad dhati: direct, via a coextensive intermediary, and via a more general intermediary. This structure organizes the masai'l of usul al-fiqh, as seen in examples like 'the book establishes the ruling definitively'.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the concept of 'arad (accident)
Understand that 'arad is any predicate external to the reality of a thing, whether essential or not. It is the 'external predicate' (al-kharij al-mahmul).
The term 'arad here is used broadly, not limited to logical accidents.
2
Distinguish 'arad dhati from 'arad gharib
Essential accidents have their source in the thing's essence; extraneous accidents do not. Only essential accidents are studied in a science.
Example: 'perception' is essential for man; 'tallness' is extraneous.
3
Memorize the three types of 'arad dhati
First: direct without intermediary (e.g., perception for man). Second: via coextensive intermediary (e.g., laughter via wonder). Third: via more general intermediary included in the reality (e.g., motion via animality).
The intermediary must be either coextensive (musawi) or more general (a'am) and inside the essence.
4
See how these are used in masai'l (issues)
Essential accidents become predicates in the issues of the science. They can be predicated on the subject of the science, on a type of the subject, or on another essential accident.
The passage gives examples from usul: 'The Book establishes the ruling definitively' and 'The command indicates obligation'.
5
Apply to usul al-fiqh examples
Analyze given attributes of usul subjects (like 'command', 'prohibition', 'general') and classify them as 'arad dhati of which type, or as extraneous.
This skill is essential for structuring usul propositions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

کے محمول بنایا جائے يقولنا الامر يفيد الوجوب الامر کتاب کا ایک نوع ہے اور یفید الوجوب عرض ذاتی ہے جو کہ محمول ہے اور علی اعراضه الذاتیة یہ تیسرا قسم ہے یعنی عرض ذاتی کو موضوع فن کے عرض ذاتی پر حمل کر کے محمول بنایا جائے گا۔
His statement: 'The subject of this science' — subject of a science is called that thing whose essential accidents are investigated in that science. 'Awarid is the plural of 'arad. What is meant by 'arad here is the definition of absolute 'arad, whether it is essential or extraneous. Summary: 'arad of a thing means that which is external to the reality of the thing and predicated on it, i.e., the external predicate. And by 'arad dhati is meant an accident for which the thing's own essence is the source, i.e., it attaches to the thing by itself without intermediary, like perception for man: perception attaches directly to man's essence without intermediary, so it is an essential accident for man. This is the first type of 'arad dhati. Or by means of something coextensive with it — this is the second type of 'arad dhati, i.e., an accident that attaches to a thing through an intermediary that is coextensive with the subject, like laughter for man: laughter attaches to man through the intermediary of wonder, and wonder is coextensive with man because every man is wonderer and every wonderer is man. Or by means of something more general than it — this is the third type of 'arad dhati, i.e., an accident that attaches to a thing through something that is more general than the thing but is included in the reality of the thing, like motion for man: motion attaches to man through animality, and animal is more general than man and is included in his reality because man is a rational animal. These three types are called 'arad dhati. Besides these, extraneous accidents ('arad gharib). In the science, only essential accidents of the subject are investigated. Meaning of investigation: that these accidents will be used in issues as predicates. When they become predicates, what will be the subject of the issue? The commentator detailed this and mentioned four types of subject of the issue. First: predication on the subject of the science — i.e., essential accidents are predicated on the subject itself. So in an issue, the predicate is an essential accident and the subject is the subject of the science, like 'The Book establishes the ruling definitively' — 'establishing ruling' is among the accidents of proofs, and it is made a predicate, and 'the Book' is the subject. Second: on its types — i.e., an essential accident is predicated on a type of the subject of the science, like our statement: 'The command indicates obligation' — 'the command' is a type of 'the Book', and 'indicates obligation' is an essential accident that is the predicate. Third: on its essential accidents — i.e., an essential accident is predicated on another essential accident of the subject of the science.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a detailed definition of 'arad (accident) and 'arad dhati (essential accident) in the context of usul al-fiqh. The commentator first clarifies that the subject of any science is that thing whose essential attributes are studied. 'Arad here means any accident, whether essential or extraneous. Essential accidents are those that stem directly from the thing's essence (first type), or through a coextensive intermediary (second type, like laughter through wonder), or through a more general intermediary included in the thing's reality (third type, like motion through animality). Only essential accidents are investigated in a science. The passage then explains how these essential accidents are used in the issues (masai'l) of the science: they become predicates, and the subject of the issue can be either the subject of the science itself, a type of it, or another essential accident. Examples from Hanafi usul are given: 'The Book establishes the ruling definitively' (predicate on the subject), 'The command indicates obligation' (predicate on a type), and presumably a third example from the text (though partly incomplete). This foundational principle determines the structure of usul al-fiqh as a science.

Key Terms
عرض ذاتی ('arad dhati): An accident that attaches to a thing by virtue of its essence, either directly (first type), via a coextensive intermediary (second), or via a more general intermediary included in the essence (third).
عرض غریب ('arad gharib): An extraneous accident that does not stem from the essence of the thing and is not investigated in the science.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi classification, which of the following is an example of the first type of 'arad dhati?
A) Laughter for man (via wonder).
B) Perception for man (directly).
C) Motion for man (via animality).
D) Being tall for man (extraneous).

Key Takeaway
The classification of 'arad dhati into three types is foundational for structuring the subject matter of any science in Hanafi methodology, including usul al-fiqh.

The Hanafi Definition of the Quran in Usul al-Fiqh
Analyzes objections to the definition of Quran as 'what is between the covers of the mushaf'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the Quran in Usul al-Fiqh, identify the two standard objections to it, and explain the commentator's defense based on the distinction between the whole and its parts.

Core Idea
The Quran's usul definition refers to the collective whole, not a universal, and using parts as proof does not invalidate it.

In Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh, the Quran is defined as 'what is transmitted between the covers of the mushaf' (ما نقل بين دفتي المصاحف). This definition, taken from the author of the matn, has been critiqued by some who argue that it either overextends (including non-Quranic fragments) or underextends (excluding parts legitimately treated as Quran, like a single verse). The commentator refutes these objections by clarifying that the definition refers to the Quran as a collective individual entity (مجموع شخصی), not a universal genus (کلی). This nuance preserves the definition's validity for usul purposes, where the scholar derives evidence from parts qua parts of the whole.

Guided Path
1
State the definition and its intended scope
Identify the phrase 'ما نقل بين دفتي المصاحف' and note that the author intends it to refer to the entire Quranic corpus as a single, indivisible unit (مجموع من حیث المجموع).
This is a 'personal individual' (شخصی) concept, not a universal (کلی) that can be divided.
2
Trace the two-pronged objection
The objection argues: if the definition is taken universally (مفہوم کلی), it falsely includes every letter and word, even those not Quranically sanctified in custom. If taken as only the complete speech (کلام مخصوص), it excludes parts like single verses that jurists treat as Quran (e.g., prohibition of touching for junub).
Both horns of the dilemma undermine either the definition's inclusivity (طرد) or its exclusivity (عکس).
3
Understand the commentator's defense of the definition
The commentator argues that the definition refers to the collective whole, not a universal. When a usuli uses a verse for deduction, he does so with the consideration that it is 'from the Book' (من کتاب), not that it is the Book itself. Thus the definition as the whole does not hinder the use of parts.
The usuli's object of study is the Quran's properties as a source of proof, which includes all its meaningful parts.
4
Connect to the purpose of Usul al-Fiqh
The usuli examines the Quran from the angle of its being a legal proof (دلیل شرعی). The definition as the transmitted text between two covers suffices because it encompasses all components (words, letters) that bear legal significance.
The commentator cites that proof is 'that which with correct consideration can lead to an informative desired end' – thus meaningful parts are naturally included.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نعلى ما هو المناسب یہ مصنف کی تعریف پر ایک قسم کا اعتراض ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ اصولی آدمی چونکہ کتاب اللہ تعالیٰ سے استدلال علی الاحکام کرتا ہے اور اس کیلئے قرآن مجید کا ہر بعض استعمال ہوتا ہے یعنی آیت یا اس کے مقدار سے عموما استدلال کرتا ہے مجموعے من حیث المجموع کو استدلال میں پیش نہیں کرتا اس لئے اصول کی غرض کے ساتھ مناسب یہ ہے کہ ما نقل بین رفتی المصاحف سے مراد عام ہو جو کل اور بعض دونوں کو شامل ہو تو پھر اس عموم کے لحاظ سے به تعریف قرآن مجید کے ہر ہر حرف اور سر کلمہ پر صادق آجائیگی حالانکہ عرف شرع میں اسے قران نہیں کہتے تو گویا حد غیر محدود پر صادق آگئی جو اس کے طرد کے منافی ہے اگر مانقل سے على المخصوص کلام نام مراد ہو تو پھر وہ جو کلام تام نہیں ہے خارج از حد ہو جائیگی لیکن اسے قرآن کہا جاتا ہے کیونکہ محدث کے لئے اس حصہ کو مس کرنا اور جنب کا تلاوۃ کرنا حرام ہے تو محدود اس کو شامل ہے اور حد شامل نہ ہوئی تو یہ عکس تعریف کے منافی ہے۔ وعلى مادل عليه سياق الجو لیکن مصنف " کے نزدیک جیسے کہ اس کی کلام دال ہے ما نقل سے مراد مجموع من حیث المجموع ہے لانه جعله تعریفا کیونکہ مصنف نے اس کو مجموع شخصی کی تعریف قرار دیا ہے اور مجموع کلی جو کہ صادق علی الکل والبعض آسکتا ہے اس کی تعریف نہیں بناتا تو اس لحاظ سے اس اشکالین سابقین میں سے کوئی اشکال وارد تو نہیں ہو سکتا لیکن یہ اصول کی غرض کے ساتھ مناسب نہیں ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ ما نقل سے مراد اگر مفہوم کلی ہو جو کل اور بعض دونوں پر صادق آتے تو پھر طر یا عکس منتقض ہو جاتا ہے اگر مانقل سے مجموع من حیث المجموع مراد ہو جو کہ شخصی درجہ ہے تو پھر یہ اصولی کی غرض کے ساتھ مناسب نہیں ہے ۔ اس اعتراض کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مصنف کی مراد ما نقل سے مجموع من حیث المجموع شخصی ہے آپ کا اعتراض کہ یہ اصولی کی غرض کے ساتھ مناسبت نہیں رکھتا ہم اسے تسلیم نہیں کرتے کیونکہ اصولی جو آیت آیت سے استدلال کرتا ہے وہ بایں حیثیت کرتا ہے کہ انہا من الكتاب لا من حيث انها نفس الكتاب و عینہ یعنی یہ آیت مستدل بها کتاب کا حصہ اور جز ہے نہ یہ کہ یہ کتاب اللہ کا عین ہے اگر مفہوم کلی مراد لیا جائے جو صادق علی الکل والبعض ہے تو بھی اعتراض وارد نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ اصولی کی غرض استدلال علی الاحکام ہے لہذا اصولی کتاب اللہ یا سنہ کے احوال سے من حیث کو نہا دلیل شرعیا سے بحث کرتا ہے اور دلیل ما یمکن التوصل بصيح النظر فيه الى مطلوب خبری کو کہتے ہیں اس لحاظ سے ضروری ہے کہ وہ کلمہ والہ ہو لہذا یہ اسم فعل حرف کو شامل ہو جائیںگی یہی وجہ ہے کہ اصولی احوال خاص عام اور مشترک و حقیقت و مجاز اور امر و نہی سے بحث کرتا ہے جو اسے استدلال کا کام دیتے ہیں لہذا ما نقل کا بعض کو شامل ہونا تعریف میں خلل نہیں ڈالتا کیونکہ دلیل کا جو مفہوم پیش کیا گیا ہے ما یمکن التوصل بصیح النظر فیہ اس صحیح النظر تمراد یہ ہے کہ اس کے احوال ثابتہ
We say what is appropriate: This is a kind of objection to the author's definition. Summary: Since a usuli person derives evidence for rulings from the Book of Allah, and for this, every part of the Noble Quran is used, i.e., he generally derives evidence from a verse or its amount, he does not present the whole as a totality in evidence. Therefore, appropriate to the purpose of usul is that 'what is between the covers of the mushaf' be intended generally, including both the whole and part. Then, by this generality, the definition would apply to every single letter and word of the Noble Quran, even though in the custom of law it is not called Quran. So the definition would apply to what is not [intended], contradicting its inclusivity. If by 'what is between the covers' the specific complete speech is meant, then what is not complete speech would be outside the definition, but it is called Quran. Because it is prohibited for a person in minor impurity to touch that part and for a junub to recite it. So the defined includes it, but the definition did not include it, contradicting the exclusivity of the definition. And based on what the context indicates: but according to the author, as his speech indicates, by 'what is between the covers' he means the total as a whole, because he made it a definition of the collective individual. And he does not make it a definition of the universal whole which can apply to both the whole and part. So from this perspective, none of the previous two objections can arise, but this is not appropriate for the purpose of usul. Summary: if by 'what is between the covers' the universal meaning is intended, which applies to both whole and part, then the definition suffers from lack of exclusivity or inclusivity. If by it the total as a whole is intended, which is of the individual level, then it is not appropriate for the usuli's purpose. The answer to this objection is that the author's intention from 'what is between the covers' is the total as an individual whole. Your objection that it is not appropriate for the usuli's purpose we do not accept, because when the usuli derives evidence from verse by verse, he does so with the consideration that they are from the Book, not that they are the Book itself and its essence. That is, this verse used as evidence is a part and portion of the Book, not that it is the very Book of Allah. If the universal meaning is taken, which applies to both whole and part, then also the objection does not arise, because the usuli's purpose is derivation of evidence for rulings. Therefore, the usuli discusses the states of the Book of Allah or the Sunnah from the perspective that they are a legal proof. And proof is defined as that which with correct consideration can lead to an informative desired end. From this perspective, it is necessary that it be a meaningful word. Hence it includes particles, verbs, and letters. This is why the usuli discusses the states of specific, general, common, reality, metaphor, command, and prohibition, which serve him for derivation. Therefore, inclusion of part in 'what is between the covers' does not harm the definition, because the meaning of proof presented is 'that which with correct consideration can lead to an informative desired end'—the correct consideration means that its established states...
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage presents and resolves objections to the standard definition of the Quran in Usul al-Fiqh: 'ما نقل بين دفتي المصاحف' (what is transmitted between the covers of the mushafs). The commentator explains that the definition is intended by the author (mujannif) to refer to the entire Quran as a collective whole (مجموع من حيث المجموع), not as a universal concept (مفهوم کلی) that would apply to every part. The objection is that usul scholars often use parts of the Quran (e.g., isolated verses) as evidence, so the definition should include both whole and part. If the definition is taken as universal, it would wrongly include every letter and word, even those not considered Quran in the legal sense. If taken as only the complete corpus, it would exclude parts that are legally treated as Quran (e.g., a single verse that a junior cannot touch). The commentator defends the author by arguing that when a usuli uses a verse for proof, he considers it as being from the Book (من الكتاب) not as the Book itself. Thus the definition as the collective whole is sufficient for usul purposes because the proof is derived from parts qua parts of the whole. Furthermore, the usuli's concern is with the properties of the Quran as a proof, including its words, which are meaningful (کلمہ والہ), so the definition's reference to the whole includes all parts without needing to list them. The passage exemplifies the Hanafi usul methodology of precise definitional analysis.

Key Terms
ما نقل بين دفتي المصاحف (ma nuqila bayna daffay al-masahif): What is transmitted between the two covers of the mushafs, i.e., the entire Quranic text as a physical collection.
مجموع من حیث المجموع (majmu' min haythu al-majmu'): The whole considered as a collective entity, not as an aggregate of independent parts.
طرد و عکس (tard wa 'aks): Inclusivity (tard: the definition covers all instances of the definiendum) and exclusivity ('aks: the definition covers only instances of the definiendum).
من الكتاب (mina al-kitab): From the Book – a phrase used to indicate that a verse is part of the Quran, not the Quran itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why does the definition 'ما نقل بين دفتي المصاحف' as a collective whole not conflict with the usuli's use of individual verses as evidence?
A) Because the usuli does not use verses at all, only the whole Quran.
B) Because when a usuli uses a verse, he treats it as part of the Book, not as the Book itself.
C) Because the definition excludes parts, so verses are not considered Quran.
D) Because the author intended the definition to be universal, covering both whole and part.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of the Quran as the collective transmitted text between two covers is defended by distinguishing the entity from its parts; parts are used as evidence because they are from the Book, not as the Book itself.

The Correct Order of Word Indications in Usul al-Fiqh
Commentary defending the author's order of word classifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct order of the four-fold classification of word indications (wad', isti'mal, zuhur, dilalah) and explain the reasoning behind the Hanafi preference for that order.

Core Idea
The correct order is: wad' → isti'mal → zuhur → dilalah, following the logical sequence from coinage to use to interpretation.

In Hanafi usul, words are classified from multiple perspectives. This lesson unpacks a commentatorial discussion on the proper sequence of these classifications. The author of the matn (Sadr al-Shari'ah) presents an order, and the commentator defends it against an alternative proposed by Fakhr al-Islam. Understanding this order is key to grasping how Hanafi jurists hierarchically treat textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four divisions
The text divides word indications into four aspects: wad' (original assignment), isti'mal (usage), zuhur (clarity/obscurity), and dilalah (mode of indication). State each in Arabic.
These are not types of words but perspectives on a single word.
2
Recognize the author's order and the signal in 'thumma'
The commentator notes that the use of 'thumma' (then) in the matn signals a sequential order. Identify which ordering is being asserted as correct.
The author's order is wad', then isti'mal, then zuhur, then dilalah.
3
Understand the rationale for the author's order
The commentator provides a reason: first a word is assigned to a meaning (wad'), then it is used in that meaning (isti'mal), then we see if the meaning is apparent or hidden (zuhur), and finally we examine the manner of indication (dilalah). Paraphrase this logical flow.
This sequence is from origin to application to interpretation.
4
Contrast with Fakhr al-Islam's order
Fakhr al-Islam placed zuhur before isti'mal. Identify his reasoning from the text (manipulation in speech has two types) and note why the commentator prefers the author's order.
The author's order is considered more systematic and correct.

م و فخر الاسلام قدم التقسيم باعتبار ظهور المعنى الم یعنی فخر الاسلام نے تقسیم باعتبار الاستعمال کو مؤخر کر دیا اور تقسیم باعتبار ظہور المعنی وخفائہ کو اس سے مقدم کر دیا علی عکس ما فعله للمصنف نظراً الى ان التصرف فی الکلام الخز یہ فخر الاسلام کی ترتیب کی وجہ ہے کہ انھوں نے ادھر نظر فرمائی کہ کلام کے اندر تصرف کرنیکی دو قسمیں ہیں ایک تصرف في اللفظ وہ ہے جعل اللفظ بحیث
His statement: 'according to its assignment (wad') for it' is an explanation of the four divisions. That is, the author has given a concise explanation of the four divisions. In the words 'thumma' (then) in the second, third, etc., divisions, there is an indication that the order as mentioned in the text is correct. Since Fakhr al-Islam's divisions do not have this order, it is indicated that the order mentioned in the text is more correct than the order of Fakhr al-Islam. Because the reason for this mentioned order is that regarding a word, first and foremost is its assignment (wad') for a meaning, then second is its usage (isti'mal) in that meaning, then after that it becomes known whether the meaning used in the word is apparent or hidden, and after that comes the discussion of what is the nature of the word's indication (dilalah) of the used meaning, i.e., whether it is in the degree of explicit wording (ibarat al-nass) or implicit indication (isharat al-nass). So the arrangement of divisions should follow this mentioned method, as the author did. And Fakhr al-Islam presented the division according to the appearance of the meaning first, i.e., he postponed the division according to usage and advanced the division according to appearance and hiddenness of meaning, opposite to what the author did, considering that the manipulation in speech has two types: one is manipulation in the wording, which is making the wording... (text cuts off).
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
Passage type: An usul rule (qā'ida) concerning the proper order of the four-fold classification of words in usul al-fiqh. The commentator is expanding on the author's (sadr al-shari'ah) statement that divisions are made according to 'wad' (assignment), 'isti'mal' (usage), 'zuhur' (clarity/obscurity), and 'dilalah' (indication). The commentator argues that the author's ordering is correct because it follows the natural sequence: first comes the original coinage of a word for a meaning (wad'), then its actual use in that meaning (isti'mal), then determining whether the intended meaning is apparent or hidden (zuhur or khafa'), and finally examining the manner of indication (whether explicit as ibarat al-nass or implicit as isharah). Fakhr al-Islam reversed the order, placing the division by clarity before the division by usage, reasoning that manipulations in speech are of two types: manipulation in wording and manipulation in meaning. However, the commentator prefers the author's order as more systematic. The text is cut off before completing Fakhr al-Islam's reasoning, but the point is clear: the author's sequence is more logical because it moves from the origin of the word to its application and then to its interpretation. This discussion is critical for understanding how Hanafi usul categorizes textual evidence.

Key Terms
وضع (wad'): The original assignment of a word to a meaning; the coinage of the word for that meaning.
استعمال (isti'mal): The actual use of a word in a specific meaning in a given context.
ظهور المعنى (zuhur al-ma'na): Whether the intended meaning from the word is apparent and clear (zahir) or hidden and ambiguous (khafi).
دلالة (dilalah): The indication of the word to its meaning; how the meaning is derived from the word.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why is the author's order preferred over Fakhr al-Islam's?
A) Because it follows the logical sequence: word assignment, usage, clarity, indication.
B) Because Fakhr al-Islam's order is too complicated.
C) Because the author's order is the only one mentioned in the Qur'an.
D) Because the commentator personally dislikes Fakhr al-Islam.

Key Takeaway
The order wad' → isti'mal → zuhur → dilalah is the correct sequence in Hanafi usul for classifying word indications, as it mirrors the logical progression from coinage to interpretation.

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy
intermediate
10 min
The Clarity Hierarchy: Zahir to Mutashabih
Defines the clarity hierarchy of lafz

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify any word according to the Hanafi clarity hierarchy and determine whether it is open to ta'wil or subject to naskh.

Core Idea
The Hanafi clarity hierarchy (zahir, nass, mufassar, muhkam) determines a text's binding force and resistance to abrogation.

Words in legal texts vary in clarity. The Hanafi school has developed a nuanced classification that tells us how firmly a word conveys its meaning and whether it can be reinterpreted or even abrogated. This lesson unpacks that hierarchy, from the most apparent (zahir) to the utterly obscure (mutashabih). Mastering this classification is essential for correctly weighing textual evidence in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish apparent vs. hidden meaning
First, determine whether the meaning of the word is apparent (zahir) or hidden (khafi). This is the primary fork in the classification.
Apparent means the meaning is clear from the word's form; hidden means the meaning is not immediately clear.
2
For apparent words: check for ta'wil
If the meaning is apparent, ask: does it admit ta'wil (interpretation)? If yes, classify as zahir (if clarity comes from form alone) or nass (if clarity needs context). If no, move to step 3.
Ta'wil is a departure from the apparent meaning based on evidence.
3
For words without ta'wil: check for naskh
If the word is not open to ta'wil, check if it can be abrogated (naskh). If yes, it is mufassar; if not, it is muhkam, the highest level of clarity.
Muhkam cannot be abrogated by any other text.
4
For hidden words: identify the source of hiddenness
Hiddenness may be due to the form itself (khafi) or other factors. Determine if the meaning can be attained with effort (mushkil), if there is hope of clarification (mujmal), or if clarification is impossible (mutashabih).
The classification depends on the possibility of understanding through reflection or external evidence.

Source Text

فان قلت خلاصہ سوال یہ کہ تقسیم سے جو اقسام پیدا ہوتے ہیں ان میں ضروری ہوتا ہے کہ ایک دوسرے کے ساتھ مختلف اور متباین ہوں جو آپس میں جمع نہ ہو سکیں ۔ نصر منتف اور یہ چیز ان اقسام میں منتفی ہے کیونکہ یہ اقسام ایک دوسرے پر صادق آتے ہیں جیسے لفظ عین مشترک تبھی ہے اور عام بھی قلت خلاصہ جواب یہ کہ یہ کوئی ایک تقسیم نہیں ہے بلکہ بحسب الاعتبارات المختلفہ یہ تقسیمات متعددہ ہیں یعنی سر ایک تقسیم دوسری سے الگ ہے لیندا تقسیمات کے جمیع اقسام میں تبائین اور اختلاف کا ہونا ضروری نہیں البتہ ہر ایک ایک تقسیم میں سے جو اقسام نکلتے ہیں ان کے مابین تباین ہونا ضروری ہے اور یہ ہماری ہر ایک موجود ہے . هذا ما تری یہ ایک نظر پیش کر کے ماقبل کو واضح کیا حاصل یہ کہ ایک تقسیم کے لحاظ سے اسم منقسم الى المعرب والمبنی ہوتا ہے اور دوسری تقسیم کے لحاظ سے معرفہ اور نکرہ کی طرف تقسیم ہوتا ہے حالانکہ معرفہ اور نکرہ دونوں یا معرب ہوتے ہیں یا مبنی البتہ ایک تقسیم سے جو اقسام نکلے ہیں وہ آپس میں جمع نہیں ہو سکتے
على انه لو جعل یہ جواب ثانی ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ اگر جمیع تقسیمات کے جمیع اقسام کو متقابل کرنا پیش نظر ہو تو پھر اختلاف حیثیات و اعتبارات ان کو مختلف کرنے میں کافی ہو گا یعنی اختلاف حیثیات اعتبار کیا جائیگا تو اس وقت جمیع اقسام متباین ہو جائیں گے کمانی اقسام مثلا تقسیم اول کے اقسام سے لفظ عین کو دیکھتے بائیں لحاظ کہ بمعنی باصرہ ہو کر جمیع افراد با صرہ کو شامل ہے تو عام ہے اگر بائیں حیثیت دیکھئے کہ اس کی وضع باصرہ کے لئے اور چشمہ سونا گھٹنا وغیرہ کے لئے ہے تو اس لحاظ سے مشترک ہے نہ عام اسی طرح یہ اقسام حیثیات کے ساتھ دوسرے کے متبائین اور مختلف ہو جاتے ہیں ہکذا التقسيم الثانی وغیرہ ۔ قوله وهذا ما قال عبر فخر الاسلام عن التقسيم الاول یعنی تقسیم اول کے متعلق فخر الاسلام کی تعبیر و عبارت یوں ہے الاول فی وجوه النظم صیغہ ولغۃ فقیل بعض حضرات نے تو یہ کہا کہ صیغہ ولغتہ مترادف اور ہم معنی ہیں جیسے کہا گیا ہے لغتہ سے لفظ کا مادہ تر کیبیہ مراد ہوتا اور صیغہ سے اس کی ہیئہ جو حرکات سکنات کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے اور ان ہی کی وجہ سے لفظ دال علی المعنی ہوتا ہے لہذا مقصود تقسیم النظم باعتبار نفس المعنی ہے جس میں متکلم اور سامع کو کوئی دخل نہیں ہے جیسے کہ بعض تقسیمات ظہور معنی یا خضار معنی باعتبار المسلم والسامع ہوتا ہے ۔ والاقرب ما ذكره المصنف فخر الاسلام کی اس تعبیر مذکور کی تفسیر جو مصنف نے اپنے الفاظ باعتبار وضعہ لہ کے ساتھ کی ہے یہ اقرب ہے تو مقصود تقسیم اللفظ باعتبار الوضع ہے۔ لان الصيغة یہ اس مراد پر دلیل ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ صیغہ اس ہیئہ کا نام ہے جو لفظ کو باعتبار حرکات و سکنات اور باعتبار ترتیب حروف یعنی بعض کو بعض پر مقدم کرنے کے لحاظ سے عارض ہوتی ہے ۔ واللغة لغت لفظ موضوع کو کہتے ہیں لیکن اس مقام پر لغہ سے مراد مادة لفظ اور جو ہر حروف ہے یعنی وہ حروف جس سے لفظ کی ترکیب و تالیف ہے۔ بقرنية انضمامه یعنی لفظ لفظ کو لفظ صیغہ کے ساتھ منضم کر کے ادھر ہی اشارہ کیا کہ لغت سے مراد ماده ترکیبیہ ہے چونکہ صیفہ سے مراد میئہ عارضہ
And by the third division: according to this division, the word is divided into zahir, nass, mufassar, muhkam and their opposites khafi, mushkil, etc. Because if the meaning of the word is apparent, then does it contain the possibility of interpretation (ta'wil) or not? If it contains the possibility of interpretation, then if its apparentness is solely and exclusively from the form (sigha), it is called zahir; otherwise it is nass. And if it does not contain the possibility of interpretation, then if it is subject to abrogation (naskh), it is mufassar; if not subject to abrogation, it is muhkam. And if the meaning is not apparent but hidden, then its hiddenness may be due to the form. Then if understanding is possible with reflection, it is called mushkil; if not possible with reflection, then if there is hope of clarification, it is called mujmal; if no hope of clarification, it is called mutashabih. And by the fourth division: according to this division, the word is divided into four types: one indicating by way of 'ibara, second by way of ishara, third by way of dalala, fourth by way of iqtida. These are the well-known types: 'ibara an-nass, ishara an-nass, dalalat an-nass, and iqtida' an-nass. Because if it indicates the meaning by the wording (nazm), then if it is brought for that very meaning and the context is for that meaning, it is called 'ibara an-nass; if it is not brought for that meaning, it is called ishara an-nass. If it indicates by the mafhum (implied meaning), meaning its indication is not by wording but by linguistic implication, then that is dalalat an-nass. And iqtida' is iqtida' an-nass. The basis of these types is induction (istiqra'), which is mentioned. Then a question: The divisions that emerge from a division must be different and mutually exclusive, not overlapping. But this condition is absent in these divisions because these divisions apply to each other, like the word 'ayn is both common (mushtarak) and general ('amm). The answer: This is not one division but multiple divisions according to different considerations. That is, each division is separate from the other. It is not necessary that all divisions be mutually exclusive; rather, within each division the categories must be mutually exclusive, and that is present in each. This is what you see: an example is presented clarifying the previous. The result is that according to one division, a noun is divided into mu'rab and mabni, and according to another division into ma'rifa and nakira, even though ma'rifa and nakira are either mu'rab or mabni. However, the categories within one division cannot be combined. A second answer: If one intends to make all divisions oppose each other, then the difference of perspectives (i'tibar) suffices to differentiate them. For example, in the first division, the word 'ayn is considered: from the perspective that it includes all individuals of 'basira' (sight), it is 'amm; from the perspective that it is placed for 'basira' and also for spring, gold, knee etc., it is mushtarak, not 'amm. Thus these categories become distinct and different through perspectives. Similarly for the other divisions. His statement: 'This is what Fakhr al-Islam said concerning the first division' — that is, Fakhr al-Islam's expression regarding the first division is as follows: 'The first (division) is concerning the aspects of nazm: sigha and lugha.' So some said that sigha and lugha are synonymous. It is said that by lugha is meant the material (madda) of the word, and by sigha is meant its form (hay'a) arising from vowels and consonants, and it is by this that the word indicates meaning. Therefore, the purpose of dividing nazm is based on the meaning itself, in which the speaker and listener have no role, unlike some divisions where apparentness or hiddenness of meaning depends on the speaker and listener. And the closer view is what the author mentioned: Fakhr al-Islam's interpretation of the mentioned expression, which the author expressed with his own words 'according to its wad'' (placement), is that the purpose is the division of the word according to wad'. Because sigha is evidence of this meaning. Summary: Sigha is the name of the form that occurs to the word in terms of vowels and consonants and in terms of the order of letters (some before others). And lugha is called the placed word, but in this context lugha refers to the material of the word and the essence of letters, i.e., the letters that compose the word. By 'inqidam' (joining) of the word to the word sigha, it is indicated that lugha means the composite material, since sigha means the accidental form.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary explains two major classifications of lafz (words) used in legal interpretation. The first classification is based on the clarity of meaning, creating a hierarchy: zahir (apparent, open to ta'wil), nass (clear, open to ta'wil but not from form alone), mufassar (clear, subject to naskh), muhkam (clear, not subject to naskh), and their opposites: khafi (hidden due to form), mushkil (hidden but attainable with effort), mujmal (hidden with hope of clarification), mutashabih (hidden without hope). The second classification is based on how the word indicates its meaning: 'ibara (direct indication by wording), ishara (indirect indication, not the primary intent), dalala (indication by implication/mafhum), and iqtida (indication by necessity). The author then addresses a potential objection that these categories overlap (e.g., 'ayn is both mushtarak and 'amm). The response clarifies that these are separate divisions based on different perspectives, so overlap is acceptable within different classifications. Finally, the author quotes Fakhr al-Islam on the distinction between sigha (form) and lugha (material), emphasizing that the division is based on wad' (linguistic assignment). This passage is essential for Hanafi usul as it provides the tools for analyzing the strength and type of textual evidence.

Key Terms
ظاہر (zahir): A word whose meaning is apparent from its form (sigha) alone and is open to interpretation (ta'wil).
نص (nass): A word whose meaning is apparent but not solely from its form; it requires context, and is open to ta'wil.
مفسر (mufassar): A word that is clear and subject to abrogation (naskh).
محکم (muhkam): A word that is clear and not subject to abrogation (naskh).
خفی (khafi): A word whose meaning is hidden due to the form itself.
مشکل (mushkil): A word whose meaning is hidden but can be understood with effort and reflection.
مجمل (mujmal): A word whose meaning is hidden but there is hope of clarification from elsewhere.
متشابہ (mutashabih): A word whose meaning is hidden with no hope of clarification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi clarity hierarchy, which two categories are both clear and not open to ta'wil?
A) Zahir and nass
B) Mufassar and muhkam
C) Khafi and mushkil
D) Mujmal and mutashabih

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi clarity hierarchy of lafz ranges from zahir (ta'wil possible) to muhkam (no ta'wil, no naskh), and from khafi to mutashabih for hidden meanings.

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy
intermediate
8 min
Modes of Indication: Ibarah, Isharah, Dalalah, Iqtida
Defines the four modes of textual indication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the four modes of textual indication (ibarah, isharah, dalalah, iqtida') and apply each in deriving legal rulings.

Core Idea
A text's legal meaning extends beyond its wording to include direct, indirect, implicative, and necessitative indications.

The Hanafi school recognizes that a single legal text can convey meaning in multiple ways. Beyond the direct meaning (ibarah), a text may also imply a secondary meaning (isharah), indicate a consequence by implication (dalalah), or require an implicit addition for its validity (iqtida'). This lesson introduces these four modes, which are essential for fully extracting rulings from the primary sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the direct meaning (ibarah)
Ask: What is the primary meaning for which the text was brought? This is the ‘ibarah an-nass, the direct indication by wording.
Example: 'وَالسَّارِقُ وَالسَّارِقَةُ فَاقْطَعُوا أَيْدِيَهُمَا' directly indicates cutting the hand of a thief.
2
Identify the indirect meaning (isharah)
If the text indicates a secondary meaning not primarily intended but understood from context, that is isharah an-nass.
Example: The command to parents not to say 'uff' (Quran 17:23) indirectly indicates the prohibition of beating them.
3
Identify the implicative meaning (dalalah)
When the text indicates a meaning by way of linguistic implication (mafhum), not by direct wording, that is dalalah an-nass.
Example: 'فَلَا تَقُل لَّهُمَا أُفٍّ' implies that striking is even more prohibited (mafhum muwafaqa).
4
Identify the necessitative meaning (iqtida')
If the text requires an implicit addition for its statement to be true or coherent, that is iqtida' an-nass.
Example: 'رَبَّنَا اصْرِفْ عَنَّا عَذَابَ جَهَنَّمَ' necessitates that 'the punishment' is understood as 'the entry into the punishment', because the statement literally means 'turn away from us the punishment of Hell' which is not coherent unless we understand 'our entering'.

على انه لو جعل یہ جواب ثانی ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ اگر جمیع تقسیمات کے جمیع اقسام کو متقابل کرنا پیش نظر ہو تو پھر اختلاف حیثیات و اعتبارات ان کو مختلف کرنے میں کافی ہو گا یعنی اختلاف حیثیات اعتبار کیا جائیگا تو اس وقت جمیع اقسام متباین ہو جائیں گے کمانی اقسام مثلا تقسیم اول کے اقسام سے لفظ عین کو دیکھتے بائیں لحاظ کہ بمعنی باصرہ ہو کر جمیع افراد با صرہ کو شامل ہے تو عام ہے اگر بائیں حیثیت دیکھئے کہ اس کی وضع باصرہ کے لئے اور چشمہ سونا گھٹنا وغیرہ کے لئے ہے تو اس لحاظ سے مشترک ہے نہ عام اسی طرح یہ اقسام حیثیات کے ساتھ دوسرے کے متبائین اور مختلف ہو جاتے ہیں ہکذا التقسيم الثانی وغیرہ ۔ قوله وهذا ما قال عبر فخر الاسلام عن التقسيم الاول یعنی تقسیم اول کے متعلق فخر الاسلام کی تعبیر و عبارت یوں ہے الاول فی وجوه النظم صیغہ ولغۃ فقیل بعض حضرات نے تو یہ کہا کہ صیغہ ولغتہ مترادف اور ہم معنی ہیں جیسے کہا گیا ہے لغتہ سے لفظ کا مادہ تر کیبیہ مراد ہوتا اور صیغہ سے اس کی ہیئہ جو حرکات سکنات کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے اور ان ہی کی وجہ سے لفظ دال علی المعنی ہوتا ہے لہذا مقصود تقسیم النظم باعتبار نفس المعنی ہے جس میں متکلم اور سامع کو کوئی دخل نہیں ہے جیسے کہ بعض تقسیمات ظہور معنی یا خضار معنی باعتبار المسلم والسامع ہوتا ہے ۔ والاقرب ما ذكره المصنف فخر الاسلام کی اس تعبیر مذکور کی تفسیر جو مصنف نے اپنے الفاظ باعتبار وضعہ لہ کے ساتھ کی ہے یہ اقرب ہے تو مقصود تقسیم اللفظ باعتبار الوضع ہے۔ لان الصيغة یہ اس مراد پر دلیل ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ صیغہ اس ہیئہ کا نام ہے جو لفظ کو باعتبار حرکات و سکنات اور باعتبار ترتیب حروف یعنی بعض کو بعض پر مقدم کرنے کے لحاظ سے عارض ہوتی ہے ۔ واللغة لغت لفظ موضوع کو کہتے ہیں لیکن اس مقام پر لغہ سے مراد مادة لفظ اور جو ہر حروف ہے یعنی وہ حروف جس سے لفظ کی ترکیب و تالیف ہے۔ بقرنية انضمامه یعنی لفظ لفظ کو لفظ صیغہ کے ساتھ منضم کر کے ادھر ہی اشارہ کیا کہ لغت سے مراد ماده ترکیبیہ ہے چونکہ صیفہ سے مراد میئہ عارضہ
And by the third division: according to this division, the word is divided into zahir, nass, mufassar, muhkam and their opposites khafi, mushkil, etc. Because if the meaning of the word is apparent, then does it contain the possibility of interpretation (ta'wil) or not? If it contains the possibility of interpretation, then if its apparentness is solely and exclusively from the form (sigha), it is called zahir; otherwise it is nass. And if it does not contain the possibility of interpretation, then if it is subject to abrogation (naskh), it is mufassar; if not subject to abrogation, it is muhkam. And if the meaning is not apparent but hidden, then its hiddenness may be due to the form. Then if understanding is possible with reflection, it is called mushkil; if not possible with reflection, then if there is hope of clarification, it is called mujmal; if no hope of clarification, it is called mutashabih. And by the fourth division: according to this division, the word is divided into four types: one indicating by way of 'ibara, second by way of ishara, third by way of dalala, fourth by way of iqtida. These are the well-known types: 'ibara an-nass, ishara an-nass, dalalat an-nass, and iqtida' an-nass. Because if it indicates the meaning by the wording (nazm), then if it is brought for that very meaning and the context is for that meaning, it is called 'ibara an-nass; if it is not brought for that meaning, it is called ishara an-nass. If it indicates by the mafhum (implied meaning), meaning its indication is not by wording but by linguistic implication, then that is dalalat an-nass. And iqtida' is iqtida' an-nass. The basis of these types is induction (istiqra'), which is mentioned. Then a question: The divisions that emerge from a division must be different and mutually exclusive, not overlapping. But this condition is absent in these divisions because these divisions apply to each other, like the word 'ayn is both common (mushtarak) and general ('amm). The answer: This is not one division but multiple divisions according to different considerations. That is, each division is separate from the other. It is not necessary that all divisions be mutually exclusive; rather, within each division the categories must be mutually exclusive, and that is present in each. This is what you see: an example is presented clarifying the previous. The result is that according to one division, a noun is divided into mu'rab and mabni, and according to another division into ma'rifa and nakira, even though ma'rifa and nakira are either mu'rab or mabni. However, the categories within one division cannot be combined. A second answer: If one intends to make all divisions oppose each other, then the difference of perspectives (i'tibar) suffices to differentiate them. For example, in the first division, the word 'ayn is considered: from the perspective that it includes all individuals of 'basira' (sight), it is 'amm; from the perspective that it is placed for 'basira' and also for spring, gold, knee etc., it is mushtarak, not 'amm. Thus these categories become distinct and different through perspectives. Similarly for the other divisions. His statement: 'This is what Fakhr al-Islam said concerning the first division' — that is, Fakhr al-Islam's expression regarding the first division is as follows: 'The first (division) is concerning the aspects of nazm: sigha and lugha.' So some said that sigha and lugha are synonymous. It is said that by lugha is meant the material (madda) of the word, and by sigha is meant its form (hay'a) arising from vowels and consonants, and it is by this that the word indicates meaning. Therefore, the purpose of dividing nazm is based on the meaning itself, in which the speaker and listener have no role, unlike some divisions where apparentness or hiddenness of meaning depends on the speaker and listener. And the closer view is what the author mentioned: Fakhr al-Islam's interpretation of the mentioned expression, which the author expressed with his own words 'according to its wad'' (placement), is that the purpose is the division of the word according to wad'. Because sigha is evidence of this meaning. Summary: Sigha is the name of the form that occurs to the word in terms of vowels and consonants and in terms of the order of letters (some before others). And lugha is called the placed word, but in this context lugha refers to the material of the word and the essence of letters, i.e., the letters that compose the word. By 'inqidam' (joining) of the word to the word sigha, it is indicated that lugha means the composite material, since sigha means the accidental form.

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary explains two major classifications of lafz (words) used in legal interpretation. The first classification is based on the clarity of meaning, creating a hierarchy: zahir (apparent, open to ta'wil), nass (clear, open to ta'wil but not from form alone), mufassar (clear, subject to naskh), muhkam (clear, not subject to naskh), and their opposites: khafi (hidden due to form), mushkil (hidden but attainable with effort), mujmal (hidden with hope of clarification), mutashabih (hidden without hope). The second classification is based on how the word indicates its meaning: 'ibara (direct indication by wording), ishara (indirect indication, not the primary intent), dalala (indication by implication/mafhum), and iqtida (indication by necessity). The author then addresses a potential objection that these categories overlap (e.g., 'ayn is both mushtarak and 'amm). The response clarifies that these are separate divisions based on different perspectives, so overlap is acceptable within different classifications. Finally, the author quotes Fakhr al-Islam on the distinction between sigha (form) and lugha (material), emphasizing that the division is based on wad' (linguistic assignment). This passage is essential for Hanafi usul as it provides the tools for analyzing the strength and type of textual evidence.

Key Terms
عبارة النص (ibara an-nass): The indication of a word by its wording (nazm) for the very meaning it was brought for.
اشارة النص (ishara an-nass): The indication of a word by its wording for a meaning not primarily intended but understood from context.
دلالة النص (dalalat an-nass): The indication of a word by its linguistic implication (mafhum), not by direct wording.
اقتضاء النص (iqtida' an-nass): The indication of a word by necessity, requiring an implicit addition to the text.

Key Takeaway
A single text can yield multiple rulings through four modes: direct wording (ibarah), contextual clue (isharah), implied meaning (dalalah), and necessary addition (iqtida').

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy
advanced
12 min
Perspectives and the Structure of Divisions
Addresses overlap objections and the foundational distinction of sigha/lugha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how multiple classifications of a word can coexist (e.g., 'amm and mushtarak) by invoking different perspectives, and you will be able to identify the role of wad' in the sigha/lugha distinction.

Core Idea
Divisions of lafz are based on different perspectives; overlapping categories are not contradictory but arise from distinct analytical angles.

A common pitfall in usul is thinking that a word belongs exclusively to one category. The Hanafi school addresses this by noting that classifications are based on various perspectives (i'tibarat). For example, the word 'ayn can be both 'amm (general) and mushtarak (homonym) depending on how you look at it. This lesson also explores the foundational distinction between sigha (form) and lugha (material) as the basis for dividing words according to wad' (linguistic assignment).

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection: overlapping categories
The text raises an objection: A division should produce mutually exclusive categories, but here categories like 'amm and mushtarak overlap. Understand why this is a problem.
Example: 'ayn is both 'amm (if considered for one meaning) and mushtarak (if considered for multiple meanings).
2
First answer: divisions are based on different perspectives
The first response is that each division is separate and based on a different perspective (i'tibar). Categories within a single division are exclusive, but across divisions they can overlap.
Analogy: A person can be both a father and a brother, but within the category of 'relation to son' he is only a father.
3
Second answer: perspective can also differentiate across divisions
If one still insists on mutual exclusivity across all divisions, the text says we can consider the perspective itself as the differentiating factor. The same word, viewed from one perspective, is 'amm; from another, it is mushtarak.
Thus, the perspective (haythiya) makes them distinct.
4
Apply the concept to sigha vs lugha
The passage quotes Fakhr al-Islam to clarify the first division of nazm: sigha (form) and lugha (material). Some thought they were synonymous, but the correct view is that they are distinct aspects: sigha is the accidental form (hay'a 'arida) bestowed by vowel/consonant arrangement, while lugha is the material (madda) of letters. This distinction is the basis for dividing words according to wad'.
The purpose is to show that the division of words is based on wad', not on speaker/hearer perceptions.

وبالتقسيم الثالث اور تیسری تقسیم کے لحاظ سے منقسم ہو گا ظاہر نص مفسر محکم اور ان کے مقابلات خفی - مشکل وغیرہ کی طرف لانه ان ظهر معناه الخ یہ وجہ تقسیم و حصر ہے کہ اگر لفظ کا معنی ظاہر ہے تو پھر اس کے اندر احتمال تاویل ہو گا یا نہیں خان احتمل التاویل اگر اس کے اندرا حتمال تاویل ہے پھر اگر اس کا ظہور معنی صرف اور محض صیغہ سے ہے تو اس کو ظاہر کہتے ہیں ورنہ تو نص وان لم يحتمل اگر احتمال تاویل نہ ہو تو پھر اگر قابل نسخ ہو تو وہ مفسر ہے اگر قابل نسخ نہ ہو تو وہ محکم ہے دان خفی معناہ یہ تقسیم الی المقابلات ہے یعنی اگر اس لفظ معنی ظاہر نہیں ہے بلکہ خفی ہے تو فاما ان یکون یعنی اس کا خفا صیغہ کی وجہ سے ہوگا پھر خان امکن اور الہ یعنی غور فکر کے ساتھ یا تو اس معنی کا ادراک ممکن ہو گا تو اسے مشکل کہتے ہیں والا یعنی غور فکر کے ساتھ اگر ادراک معنی ممکن نہیں ہے تو فان كان البیان پھر اگر تبیین اور توضیح معنی کی امید در جا ہے تو تو اس کو مجمل کہتے ہیں اگر امید بیان نہیں ہے تو اس کو متشابہ کہتے ہیں وبالتقسيم الرابع یعنی تقسیم رابع کے لحاظ سے لفظ منقسم ہو گا اربعہ اقسام کی طرف ایک دال بطريق العبارة دوسرا دال بطريق الاشارہ تیسرا قسم وال بطریق الدلالہ چوتھا دال بطریق الاقتضا یہ وہی مشہور اقسام ہیں عبارة النص - اشارة النص - دلالۃ النص اور اقتضاء النص لانه ان دل على المعنى بالنظم یہ وجہ تقسیم و حصر ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ لفظ اگر دال علی المعنی بالنظم ہے پھر اگر وہ اسی معنی مدلول کی خاطر مسوق ہے اور سیاق کلام اسی معنی کے لئے ہے تو اسے عبارة النص کہتے ہیں اگر اس کی خاطر مسوق نہیں ہے تو اسے اشارۃ النص کہتے ہیں ۔ فان دل عليه بالمفهوم یعنی اگر اس لفظ کی دلالت بالنظم واللفظ نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کی دلالت باعتبار مفہوم لغوی کے ہے تو وہ دلالة النص والاقتضاء الى اقتضاء النص والعمدة اصل شئی تو ان اقسام کے متعلق استقراء ہے جو مذکور ہے ۔
فان قلت خلاصہ سوال یہ کہ تقسیم سے جو اقسام پیدا ہوتے ہیں ان میں ضروری ہوتا ہے کہ ایک دوسرے کے ساتھ مختلف اور متباین ہوں جو آپس میں جمع نہ ہو سکیں ۔ نصر منتف اور یہ چیز ان اقسام میں منتفی ہے کیونکہ یہ اقسام ایک دوسرے پر صادق آتے ہیں جیسے لفظ عین مشترک تبھی ہے اور عام بھی قلت خلاصہ جواب یہ کہ یہ کوئی ایک تقسیم نہیں ہے بلکہ بحسب الاعتبارات المختلفہ یہ تقسیمات متعددہ ہیں یعنی سر ایک تقسیم دوسری سے الگ ہے لیندا تقسیمات کے جمیع اقسام میں تبائین اور اختلاف کا ہونا ضروری نہیں البتہ ہر ایک ایک تقسیم میں سے جو اقسام نکلتے ہیں ان کے مابین تباین ہونا ضروری ہے اور یہ ہماری ہر ایک موجود ہے . هذا ما تری یہ ایک نظر پیش کر کے ماقبل کو واضح کیا حاصل یہ کہ ایک تقسیم کے لحاظ سے اسم منقسم الى المعرب والمبنی ہوتا ہے اور دوسری تقسیم کے لحاظ سے معرفہ اور نکرہ کی طرف تقسیم ہوتا ہے حالانکہ معرفہ اور نکرہ دونوں یا معرب ہوتے ہیں یا مبنی البتہ ایک تقسیم سے جو اقسام نکلے ہیں وہ آپس میں جمع نہیں ہو سکتے
على انه لو جعل یہ جواب ثانی ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ اگر جمیع تقسیمات کے جمیع اقسام کو متقابل کرنا پیش نظر ہو تو پھر اختلاف حیثیات و اعتبارات ان کو مختلف کرنے میں کافی ہو گا یعنی اختلاف حیثیات اعتبار کیا جائیگا تو اس وقت جمیع اقسام متباین ہو جائیں گے کمانی اقسام مثلا تقسیم اول کے اقسام سے لفظ عین کو دیکھتے بائیں لحاظ کہ بمعنی باصرہ ہو کر جمیع افراد با صرہ کو شامل ہے تو عام ہے اگر بائیں حیثیت دیکھئے کہ اس کی وضع باصرہ کے لئے اور چشمہ سونا گھٹنا وغیرہ کے لئے ہے تو اس لحاظ سے مشترک ہے نہ عام اسی طرح یہ اقسام حیثیات کے ساتھ دوسرے کے متبائین اور مختلف ہو جاتے ہیں ہکذا التقسيم الثانی وغیرہ ۔ قوله وهذا ما قال عبر فخر الاسلام عن التقسيم الاول یعنی تقسیم اول کے متعلق فخر الاسلام کی تعبیر و عبارت یوں ہے الاول فی وجوه النظم صیغہ ولغۃ فقیل بعض حضرات نے تو یہ کہا کہ صیغہ ولغتہ مترادف اور ہم معنی ہیں جیسے کہا گیا ہے لغتہ سے لفظ کا مادہ تر کیبیہ مراد ہوتا اور صیغہ سے اس کی ہیئہ جو حرکات سکنات کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے اور ان ہی کی وجہ سے لفظ دال علی المعنی ہوتا ہے لہذا مقصود تقسیم النظم باعتبار نفس المعنی ہے جس میں متکلم اور سامع کو کوئی دخل نہیں ہے جیسے کہ بعض تقسیمات ظہور معنی یا خضار معنی باعتبار المسلم والسامع ہوتا ہے ۔ والاقرب ما ذكره المصنف فخر الاسلام کی اس تعبیر مذکور کی تفسیر جو مصنف نے اپنے الفاظ باعتبار وضعہ لہ کے ساتھ کی ہے یہ اقرب ہے تو مقصود تقسیم اللفظ باعتبار الوضع ہے۔ لان الصيغة یہ اس مراد پر دلیل ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ صیغہ اس ہیئہ کا نام ہے جو لفظ کو باعتبار حرکات و سکنات اور باعتبار ترتیب حروف یعنی بعض کو بعض پر مقدم کرنے کے لحاظ سے عارض ہوتی ہے ۔ واللغة لغت لفظ موضوع کو کہتے ہیں لیکن اس مقام پر لغہ سے مراد مادة لفظ اور جو ہر حروف ہے یعنی وہ حروف جس سے لفظ کی ترکیب و تالیف ہے۔ بقرنية انضمامه یعنی لفظ لفظ کو لفظ صیغہ کے ساتھ منضم کر کے ادھر ہی اشارہ کیا کہ لغت سے مراد ماده ترکیبیہ ہے چونکہ صیفہ سے مراد میئہ عارضہ
And by the third division: according to this division, the word is divided into zahir, nass, mufassar, muhkam and their opposites khafi, mushkil, etc. Because if the meaning of the word is apparent, then does it contain the possibility of interpretation (ta'wil) or not? If it contains the possibility of interpretation, then if its apparentness is solely and exclusively from the form (sigha), it is called zahir; otherwise it is nass. And if it does not contain the possibility of interpretation, then if it is subject to abrogation (naskh), it is mufassar; if not subject to abrogation, it is muhkam. And if the meaning is not apparent but hidden, then its hiddenness may be due to the form. Then if understanding is possible with reflection, it is called mushkil; if not possible with reflection, then if there is hope of clarification, it is called mujmal; if no hope of clarification, it is called mutashabih. And by the fourth division: according to this division, the word is divided into four types: one indicating by way of 'ibara, second by way of ishara, third by way of dalala, fourth by way of iqtida. These are the well-known types: 'ibara an-nass, ishara an-nass, dalalat an-nass, and iqtida' an-nass. Because if it indicates the meaning by the wording (nazm), then if it is brought for that very meaning and the context is for that meaning, it is called 'ibara an-nass; if it is not brought for that meaning, it is called ishara an-nass. If it indicates by the mafhum (implied meaning), meaning its indication is not by wording but by linguistic implication, then that is dalalat an-nass. And iqtida' is iqtida' an-nass. The basis of these types is induction (istiqra'), which is mentioned. Then a question: The divisions that emerge from a division must be different and mutually exclusive, not overlapping. But this condition is absent in these divisions because these divisions apply to each other, like the word 'ayn is both common (mushtarak) and general ('amm). The answer: This is not one division but multiple divisions according to different considerations. That is, each division is separate from the other. It is not necessary that all divisions be mutually exclusive; rather, within each division the categories must be mutually exclusive, and that is present in each. This is what you see: an example is presented clarifying the previous. The result is that according to one division, a noun is divided into mu'rab and mabni, and according to another division into ma'rifa and nakira, even though ma'rifa and nakira are either mu'rab or mabni. However, the categories within one division cannot be combined. A second answer: If one intends to make all divisions oppose each other, then the difference of perspectives (i'tibar) suffices to differentiate them. For example, in the first division, the word 'ayn is considered: from the perspective that it includes all individuals of 'basira' (sight), it is 'amm; from the perspective that it is placed for 'basira' and also for spring, gold, knee etc., it is mushtarak, not 'amm. Thus these categories become distinct and different through perspectives. Similarly for the other divisions. His statement: 'This is what Fakhr al-Islam said concerning the first division' — that is, Fakhr al-Islam's expression regarding the first division is as follows: 'The first (division) is concerning the aspects of nazm: sigha and lugha.' So some said that sigha and lugha are synonymous. It is said that by lugha is meant the material (madda) of the word, and by sigha is meant its form (hay'a) arising from vowels and consonants, and it is by this that the word indicates meaning. Therefore, the purpose of dividing nazm is based on the meaning itself, in which the speaker and listener have no role, unlike some divisions where apparentness or hiddenness of meaning depends on the speaker and listener. And the closer view is what the author mentioned: Fakhr al-Islam's interpretation of the mentioned expression, which the author expressed with his own words 'according to its wad'' (placement), is that the purpose is the division of the word according to wad'. Because sigha is evidence of this meaning. Summary: Sigha is the name of the form that occurs to the word in terms of vowels and consonants and in terms of the order of letters (some before others). And lugha is called the placed word, but in this context lugha refers to the material of the word and the essence of letters, i.e., the letters that compose the word. By 'inqidam' (joining) of the word to the word sigha, it is indicated that lugha means the composite material, since sigha means the accidental form.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary explains two major classifications of lafz (words) used in legal interpretation. The first classification is based on the clarity of meaning, creating a hierarchy: zahir (apparent, open to ta'wil), nass (clear, open to ta'wil but not from form alone), mufassar (clear, subject to naskh), muhkam (clear, not subject to naskh), and their opposites: khafi (hidden due to form), mushkil (hidden but attainable with effort), mujmal (hidden with hope of clarification), mutashabih (hidden without hope). The second classification is based on how the word indicates its meaning: 'ibara (direct indication by wording), ishara (indirect indication, not the primary intent), dalala (indication by implication/mafhum), and iqtida (indication by necessity). The author then addresses a potential objection that these categories overlap (e.g., 'ayn is both mushtarak and 'amm). The response clarifies that these are separate divisions based on different perspectives, so overlap is acceptable within different classifications. Finally, the author quotes Fakhr al-Islam on the distinction between sigha (form) and lugha (material), emphasizing that the division is based on wad' (linguistic assignment). This passage is essential for Hanafi usul as it provides the tools for analyzing the strength and type of textual evidence.

Key Terms
صیغہ (sigha): The form (hay'a) of a word, including its vowels, consonants, and order of letters.
لغت (lugha): In this context, the material (madda) or letters that compose the word; the lexical substance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for dividing words into sigha and lugha?
A) The speaker's intention
B) The listener's understanding
C) The wad' (linguistic assignment) of the word
D) The context of revelation

Key Takeaway
Multiple classifications of a word are possible and non-contradictory when they arise from different perspectives; the sigha/lugha distinction underlies the division based on wad'.

Definition of Muawwal and Its Conditions in Hanafi Usul
Defining muawwal and addressing objections about its scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define muawwal, identify its two essential conditions, and apply them to distinguish muawwal from tafsir and other categories of textual interpretation.

Core Idea
Muawwal is a common word whose meaning is chosen by predominant opinion through ijtihad — it belongs to the divisions of nazm in form and language.

This lesson unpacks the precise Hanafi definition of muawwal (the interpretable) as one of the four divisions of discourse (nazm) based on form and language. You will learn that muawwal is not any interpretation, but a specific category requiring a common (mushtarak) word and preponderance achieved by predominant opinion (ghalib al-ray) through contemplation of the expression itself. We will also address two common objections to this definition and see how the Hanafi school defends its scope using a classic fiqh example from the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of muawwal
Locate Fakhr al-Islam's statement: muawwal is a mushtarak word whose aspects are given preponderance by predominant opinion. Note the two conditions: mushtarak and tarjih bi ghalib al-ray.
This definition is the starting point for the whole passage.
2
Analyze the first objection and response
The objection: muawwal can come from non-common words (e.g., khafi, mushkil). The response: the definition is restricted to muawwal as a division of nazm (form and language), not absolute muawwal. For muawwal to belong to nazm, the word must be mushtarak.
This clarifies that the definition is not universal but specific to a classification system.
3
Analyze the second objection and response
The objection: preponderance can occur without predominant opinion, e.g., by khabar wahid or qiyas. The response: 'predominant opinion' (ghalib al-ray) here means dominant probability (zann ghalib), which includes khabar wahid, qiyas, and contemplation of the expression.
This broadens the meaning of ghalib al-ray to cover any method producing strong probability.
4
Work through the qur example
Apply the definition to the Hanafi and Shafi'i interpretations of 'qur' in Quran 2:228. Both sides consider their interpretation muawwal because they use linguistic contemplation to give preponderance to one meaning over another – the word is mushtarak and the preponderance is by predominant opinion.
This example shows muawwal in action across madhahib.
5
Confirm why muawwal belongs to nazm
Even though muawwal results from ijtihad, the ruling is still attributed to the form of the expression. Hence it is counted among the divisions of nazm based on form and language.
This addresses why muawwal is a qism of nazm despite involving ijtihad.

حقیقی معنی میں مستعمل ہے لہذا وہ عام ہو گا نہ کہ واسطہ بین العام والخاص قوله او باعتبار النوع كوجل وفرس اشارة الخ یعنی ان دو مثالوں کے اندر مصنف نے اشارہ کیا کہ عرف شریعت کا نوع یعنی نوع شرعی کبھی وہی نوع منطقی ہوتا ہے جیسے فرس اور کبھی وہ نوع منطقی نہیں ہوتا جیسے رجل فان الشرع کیونکہ شریعت رجل اور مرآۃ کو نو عین مختلفین قرار دیتی ہے ۔ نظر الی اختصاص الا یعنی شریعت کی نگاہ میں اختلاف انواع کی مدار اختلاف اغراض پر ہے چونکہ رجل کی پیدائش کے اغراض یہ ہیں کہ وہ بنی ہو اور امامتہ کبری و صغریٰ اور شہادۃ فی الحدود والقصاص یہ امور مختص بالرحل ہیں اور عورت یہ احکام نہیں رکھتی اس لئے ان خصوصیات کے اختلاف کی وجہ سے رجل الگ نوع ہے اور عورت الگ نوع ہے ۔

قولہ ثم المشترك فخر الاسلام وغیرہ نے نظم کے اقسام باعتبار صیغہ ولغہ کے چار ذکر کئے ہیں خاص - عام - مشترک - ماول - وفسر الماول تفسیر کرتے ہوئے فرمایا مشترک کے وجوہ اور معانی میں سے بعض کو غالب رأی کے ساتھ ترجیح حاصل ہو جائے تو وہ ماول کہلاتا ہے واورد علیہ اور ان کی اس تفسیر کے اوپر اولاً یہ اشکال وارد ہوتا ہے کہ یہ ضروری نہیں ہے کہ ماول ہمیشہ مشترک میں سے ہو بلکہ کبھی غیر مشترک میں سے بھی ہوتا ہے اور ثانیاً یہ کہ بعض وجوہ کی ترجیح کبھی غالب رای کے علاوہ دوسری اشیاء سے بھی ہو جاتی ہے اور وہ بھی ماول ہے ۔ کما ذکر فی المیزان جیسے میزان میں مذکور ہے کہ خفی اور مشکل اور مشترک و مجمل جب ان کی تبیین و بیان دلیل قطعی کے ساتھ حاصل ہو جائے تو یہ مفسر کہلاتا ہے اور ان کا خفا کی ایسی دلیل سے زائل ہو جائے جس میں شبہ کی گنجائش ہو جیسے خبر واحد یا قیاس تو اسکو ماول کہا جاتا ہے تو ماول مشترک کے علاوہ خفی مشکل وغیرہ سے بھی ہو جاتا ہے اور ترجیح غالب رائے کے علاوہ خبر واحد سے بھی حاصل ہو جاتی ہے واجیب عن الاول پہلے اشکال سے یہ جواب دیا گیا ہے کہ یہ تفسیر مطلق ماول کی نہیں ہے بلکہ اس ماول سے مراد وہی ماول ہے جو مشترک میں سے ہو کر اس کے بعض وجوہ ترجیح حاصل کر جائیں۔ وعن الثانی اور اشکال ثانی سے یہ جواب دیا گیا ہے کہ کہ غالب رأی سے ہماری مراد ظن غالب ہے خواہ خبر واحد سے حاصل ہو یا قیاس سے یا نا تمل فی الصیغہ سے جیسے بھی ہو اس کو غالب رائے کہا جاتا ہے اسی غالب رائے کے ساتھ ترجیح حاصل ہو جائے تو وہ ماؤل ہو جائیگا ۔ کمانی ثلثة قروء جیسے ثلاثہ قروء میں حنفیہ نے جو ہر کلمہ میں تامل کیا کہ اس لفظ کی وضع معنی اجتماع کے لئے ہے جیسے قراۃ کہ اس میں بھی اجتماع حروف کلمات ہوتا ہے اور یہ معنی مناسب حیض ہے کہ مدت طہر میں جمع ہوتا رہتا ہے بعد الاجتماع اس کا خروج ہوتا ہے اور شافعیہ نے لفظ ثلثہ کی تاثے تانیث پر نگاہ رکھی کہ اس کی تمیز حسب ضابطہ مذکر ہونی چاہیے اور یہ طہر ہے لہذا فریقین کے نزدیک یہ ماڈل ہے۔

ر معنى كونه من اقسام النظم چونکہ ماول اجتہاد کے بعد حاصل ہوتا ہے کیونکہ غالب رائے تو مجتہد ہی قائم کر سکتا ہے جب اجتہاد مجتہد کے ساتھ اس کا تحقق ہوا تو یہ اقسام نظم صيغة ولغہ سے نہیں ہو سکتا اس لئے شارح نے جوابا کہا کہ چونکہ حکم بعد از تاویل بھی منسوب الى صيغة اللفظ رہتا ہے تو اس لئے اس کو تعلق نظم کے ساتھ باعتبار صیغہ لغتہ کے ہو گیا تو اس لئے اس کو اقسام نظم میں شمار کرنا صحیح ہوگا ۔ قبل المراد بغالب الرأس الخ یہ اس سابق اشکال جو قید اشتراک اور قید ترجیح بغالب الرأی پر وارد کیا تھا یہ اس کا جواب ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ ماؤں کی جو یہ تعریف کی گئی ہے " ما ترجیح من المشترك بعض وجوہ بغالب الرأی " یہ اس ماوں کی تعریف ہے جو نظم صیغہ ولغۃ کے اقسام سے ہے اور ان اقسام میں سے ہونے کیلئے یہ دونوں شروط ضروری ہیں ایک قید اشتراک دوسری ترجیح بالاجتهاد والتأمل في نفس الصيغة یہ وہی ترجیح بغالب الرأسی کی تفسیر ہے ۔ خان المشترك یہ قید اشتراک کے ضروری ہونیکی وجہ ہے یعنی چونکہ مشترک معانی متعددہ کے لئے موضوع ہوتا ہے اور ہر معنی کا علی سبیل البدل احتمال رکھتا ہے تو جب کسی ایک معنی پر صیغہ میں غور فکر کرکے محمول کیا جائے تو یہی لفظ موضوع کا معنی متعین کرنا ہوا تو اب اس وقت یقینا اقسام نظم صیف- ولغۃ میں درج رہیگا اس سے خارج نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اس کا تعلق لفظ سے باعتبار وضع کے ہو گا بخلاف اس صورت کئے کہ جب مشترک کہ کسی ایک معنی پر دلیل قطعی کی وجہ سے محمول کیا جائے تو یہ اس کی تفسیر ہوگی تاویل نہیں ہوگی اگر خبر واحد یا قیاس کی وجہ سے کسی ایک معنی پر محمول کیا جائے تو یہ نظم صیغة ولغۃ کے اقسام سے نہیں ہو گا کیونکہ اس وقت لفظ کی وضع ملحوظ نہیں ہے اور اسی طرح جب لفظ مشترک نہیں ہے بلکہ خفی مشکل ۔ مجمل ہے تو جب اس کا خفا دلیل قطعی بالینی کے ساتھ زائل ہو تو اس میں وضع کو دخل نہ ہوا لہذا یہ بھی نظم لغۃ وصیغہ کے اقسام سے نہیں ہو سکتا اس وقت صیغہ ولغہ جس سے وضع مراد ہے اس کو دخل نہ ہوا لہذا یہ اس تقسیم مذکورہ کے اقسام میں داخل نہیں ہو گا لہذا قید اشتراک اور ترجیح بغالب الرأسی کی قید
It is used in its literal meaning, so it is general, not intermediate between general and specific. His statement: 'or according to type like man and horse' indicates that in these two examples the author pointed out that the type in Shariah (i.e., the Sharia-based type) is sometimes the same as the logical type, like horse, and sometimes it is not the logical type, like man. Because Shariah considers man and woman as two different types. Considering the specification of... i.e., in the view of Shariah, the basis of difference in types is the difference in purposes. Since the purposes of the creation of a man are that he is a son, and the greater and lesser imamate, and testimony in hadd and qisas punishments – these matters are specific to men, and a woman does not have these rulings. Therefore, due to the difference in these specificities, man is a separate type and woman is a separate type.

His statement: 'Then the common (mushtarak)'. Fakhr al-Islam and others mentioned four divisions of discourse with respect to form and language: specific, general, common (mushtarak), and muawwal. He explained muawwal: when among the aspects and meanings of a common word, some are given preponderance by predominant opinion, that is called muawwal. An objection was raised against this interpretation: first, it is not necessary that muawwal is always from among common words, rather sometimes it is from non-common words. Second, sometimes preponderance of some aspects is achieved by something other than predominant opinion, and that is also muawwal. As mentioned in al-Mizan: when khafi, mushkil, mushtarak, and mujmal are clarified by a definitive proof, they are called mufassar; but if their obscurity is removed by a proof that admits doubt, like khabar wahid or qiyas, then that is called muawwal. So muawwal can be from khafi, mushkil, etc. in addition to mushtarak, and preponderance can be achieved by khabar wahid besides predominant opinion.

The first objection was answered: this interpretation is not for muawwal absolutely, but rather the muawwal intended is that which is from among common words and some of its aspects are given preponderance. The second objection was answered: by predominant opinion we mean dominant probability (zann ghalib), whether it is from khabar wahid, qiyas, or contemplation of the expression (tamal fi al-sigha); this is called predominant opinion. If preponderance is achieved by this predominant opinion, then that is muawwal. For example, in the case of 'three periods' (thalathatu quru), the Hanafis contemplated each word: the word 'quroo' is placed for the meaning of collection, like 'qira'ah' which also comprises collection of letters and words, and this meaning is appropriate for menstruation because blood collects during the period of purity, then after collection it exits. The Shafi'is considered the femininity of the word 'thaltha' (three) because its distinguishing noun should be masculine according to the rule, and this (quroo) is purity. So from the perspective of both parties, this is muawwal.

Regarding the meaning of it being among the divisions of discourse: since muawwal is achieved after ijtihad (because only a mujtahid can establish predominant opinion), and when it is actualized by the ijtihad of a mujtahid, it cannot be from the divisions of discourse based on form and language. Therefore, the commentator answered: since the ruling after tawil is still attributed to the form of the expression, it has a connection to discourse with respect to form and language, so it is correct to count it among the divisions of discourse.

He said: 'The meaning of predominant opinion...' This is the answer to the earlier objection raised regarding the condition of mushtarak and the condition of preponderance by predominant opinion. In summary, the definition of muawwal given as 'that which is from the common word, some of its aspects are given preponderance by predominant opinion' is the definition of the muawwal that is among the divisions of discourse in form and language. To be among these divisions, these two conditions are necessary: one, the condition of mushtarak; two, preponderance by ijtihad and contemplation (tamal) in the expression itself – this is the interpretation of preponderance by predominant opinion. The condition of mushtarak is necessary because a common word is placed for multiple meanings, each meaning being possible on a substitutional basis. When it is interpreted to one meaning by contemplation and reflection in the expression, then this is specifying the meaning of the word as placed, so it certainly falls within the divisions of discourse in form and language; it does not exit from it, because its connection is to the word with respect to its placement. In contrast, if a common word is interpreted to one meaning by a definitive proof, that is tafsir (interpretation), not tawil. If it is interpreted to one meaning by khabar wahid or qiyas, then it does not fall under the divisions of discourse in form and language, because at that time the placement of the word is not considered. Similarly, when the word is not common but khafi, mushkil, or mujmal, if its obscurity is removed by a definitive proof, then placement is not involved, so this also cannot be among the divisions of discourse in form and language. At that time, form and language (by which placement is meant) are not involved, so it is not included in the said divisions. Therefore, the condition of mushtarak and the condition of preponderance by predominant opinion are necessary.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the definition of muawwal (interpretable) within Hanafi usul al-fiqh, specifically addressing its status as one of the four divisions of discourse (nazm) based on form and language (sigha wa lugha). The author begins with examples of types in Shariah, showing how legal types can differ from logical types (e.g., man vs. woman). Moving to the core, he cites Fakhr al-Islam's definition: muawwal is a common (mushtarak) word whose aspects are given preponderance by predominant opinion (ghalib al-ray). Two objections are raised: (1) muawwal can also be from non-common words like khafi or mushkil; (2) preponderance can occur without predominant opinion, e.g., through khabar wahid or qiyas. The answer clarifies that the definition is specific to muawwal as a division of nazm based on form and language, not absolute muawwal. The first objection is deflected by restricting the definition to mushtarak words. The second is resolved by explaining that 'predominant opinion' here means dominant probability (zann ghalib), which can arise from various sources including khabar wahid and qiyas. A concrete fiqh example is given: the Hanafi interpretation of 'three periods' (qur' in Quran 2:228) as menstrual periods, based on contemplating the word 'quru' as meaning collection, whereas Shafi'is consider it as purity due to the femininity of 'three' requiring a masculine distinguishing noun. Both interpretations are considered muawwal. The passage then addresses why muawwal is counted among the divisions of nazm: because the ruling after tawil is still attributed to the expression's form. The two conditions for this category are reaffirmed: the word must be mushtarak, and the preponderance must be achieved through ijtihad and contemplation within the expression itself, not through external definitive proof. This ensures that the process remains tied to the word's literal placement.

Key Terms
ماول (muawwal): A common (mushtarak) word whose aspects are given preponderance by predominant opinion (ghalib al-ray) through ijtihad and contemplation of the expression itself.
غالب الرأي (ghalib al-ray): Predominant opinion or dominant probability (zann ghalib) that can arise from various sources such as khabar wahid, qiyas, or contemplation of the expression itself.
مشترك (mushtarak): A word that is placed (wad') for multiple meanings on a substitutional basis (ala sabili al-badal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the two necessary conditions for a word to be classified as muawwal within the Hanafi divisions of discourse (nazm)?
A) The word must be mushtarak and preponderance must be by predominant opinion through ijtihad in the expression itself.
B) The word must be khafi or mushkil, and preponderance must be by definitive proof.
C) The word must be general (amm) and preponderance must be by qiyas.
D) The word must be specific (khass) and preponderance must be by consensus.

Key Takeaway
Muawwal in Hanafi usul is a defined category: a common word whose interpretation is reached by predominant opinion through ijtihad in the expression itself, distinguishing it from tafsir and from interpretations using external proofs.
