Categories of Ambiguous Texts: Khafi, Mushkil, Mujmal, and Mutashabih
Defines mutashabih and provides rulings for ambiguous texts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between khafi, mushkil, mujmal, and mutashabih and state the Hanafi procedural ruling for each.

Core Idea
Each level of textual ambiguity demands a distinct response: from inquiry to suspension.

In Hanafi usul, not all unclear texts are treated the same. The school categorizes ambiguity into four levels, each with a prescribed method of resolution. This lesson equips you to identify which type you face and apply the correct usul procedure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of ambiguity
Determine why the text is unclear: Is it due to a subtle hidden meaning (khafi), a conflict or difficulty (mushkil), an ambiguous word requiring definition (mujmal), or a meaning beyond human comprehension (mutashabih)?
Khafi can be resolved with little thought; mushkil requires ijtihad.
2
Match to the correct category
Using the examples from the text, classify the ambiguity. For instance, the disconnected letters (muqatta'at) are mutashabih; the word 'salat' before explanation is mujmal.
The categories are hierarchical in clarity: mutashabih is the least clear; khafi is the most clear among the ambiguous.
3
Apply the Hanafi ruling
For khafi: talab (inquiry). For mushkil: talab then ta'mmul (reflection). For mujmal: istifsar (asking for clarification). For mutashabih: tawaqquf (suspension of interpretation).
Mutashabih is accepted as true without specifying the modality.
4
Understand the practical difference
The ruling determines whether a mujtahid may engage ijtihad or must refrain. For example, mutashabih verses on divine attributes are not subject to ta'wil.
This preserves the Salaf methodology of tafwid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمتشابہ کالمقطعات في اوائل السور الخ متشابہہ کی چند مثالیں پیش کر دیں جیسے اوائل سور میں مقطعات اور جیسے اللہ تعالیٰ کے لئے اثبات ید اور اثبات وجہ و نحو ما اسی مثل العين والقدم والسمع والبصر. وحكم المخفي الخز یہاں سے ان کا حکم پیش کر دیا کہ خفی کا حکم ہے الطلب یعنی فکر قلیل اور یہ معلوم کرنا کہ خفا مزیتہ و زیادہ کی وجہ سے ہے یا نقص و ضعف کی وجہ پھر اس کے مناسب جریان حكم والمشكل الطلب ثم التامل تأمل سے مراد ہے التکلف والاجتہاد فی الفکر تاکہ اس کا معنی اشکال سے عمیرہ ہو جائے . والمجمل الاستفسار اور مجمل کی تبیین چونکہ بالنقل ہوتی ہے اس لئے پہلے استفسار ضروری ہے یعنی طلب البیان عن المجمل یعنی اجمال کنندہ سے طلب کیا جائے کہ وہ خود اسے بیان کرے اور اس کی وضاحت کرے اور کبھی یہ بیان شافی وافی سے جس کے ساتھ ابہام و خفا پوری طرح مرتفع ہو جاتا ہے اس وقت وہ مجمل مفسر ہو جاتا ہے جیسے صلوۃ زکوۃ مجمل تھے لیکن ان کی تبیین و توضیح علی طریقہ الکمال ہو چکی ہے اب یہ مفسر ہیں اور کبھی بیاں غیر شانی ہوتا ہے جیسے بیان ریوا جو اس حدیث کے ساتھ ہوا ہے جو اشیاء ستہ میں وارد ہے حضرت عمراض نے فرمایا خرج النبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم من الدنيا ولم يبين لنا ابواب الربوا اس وقت ضرورت ہوتی ہے کہ صاف اوصاف صالح للعلیہ کی جستجو کی جائے اور ان علل کی بنیاد پر تامل کر کے احکام جاری کئے جائیں جیسے کہ مجتہدین نے ریوا کے بارہ میں کیا۔

والمتشابه التوقف فهذا من باب العطف یعنی یہ عبارت از قبیله عطف علی معمولی عاملین مختلفین سے ہے اور عاطف واحد ہے کیونکہ لفظ المتشابہ کا عطف لفظ الخفی
And 'mutashabih' is like the disconnected letters at the beginnings of chapters. Several examples of mutashabih are presented: the disconnected letters at the beginnings of surahs, and like the affirmation of 'hand' and 'face' for Allah, and similar to that, such as 'eye', 'foot', 'hearing', and 'sight'. And the ruling of khafi: its ruling is inquiry (talab), meaning little thought, and to know whether the hiddenness is due to superiority or deficiency, then apply the ruling accordingly. And mushkil: inquiry then reflection (ta'mmul), where reflection means exertion and ijtihad in thought so that its meaning becomes free from ambiguity. And mujmal: asking for clarification (istifsar), because clarification of mujmal is by transmission, so first asking for explanation is necessary, i.e., asking the one who made it mujmal to explain it. And sometimes this explanation is sufficient and complete, by which ambiguity and hiddenness are fully removed; then the mujmal becomes clear (mufassar), like 'salat' and 'zakat' were mujmal, but their explanation and clarification have been perfected, so now they are clear. And sometimes the explanation is not such, like the explanation of riba by the hadith on the six items. 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'The Prophet left this world without explaining to us the doors of riba.' At that time, it is necessary to search for the clear attributes suitable for the cause, and based on those causes, to reflect and issue rulings, as the mujtahids did regarding riba. And regarding mutashabih: suspension (tawaqquf); this is from the category of conjunction with one particle connecting different operators, because the word 'mutashabih' is conjoined to the word 'khafi'.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage continues the analysis of ambiguous texts by defining mutashabih and providing the ruling for each category. Mutashabih texts are those that are ambiguous due to their content being beyond human understanding, such as the disconnected letters at the beginnings of surahs and the anthropomorphic attributes of Allah. The ruling for mutashabih is tawaqquf (suspension of judgment). The passage also summarizes the rulings for the other categories: khafi (hidden due to a subtle reason, ruling: inquiry), mushkil (problematic, ruling: inquiry followed by reflection/ta'mmul), and mujmal (ambiguous due to the word itself, ruling: ask for clarification from the Lawgiver). The example of riba is revisited to show that when the clarification is not comprehensive, analogy (qiyas) is used to extend the ruling. The final sentence is a grammatical note about the conjunction structure.

Key Terms
متشابه (mutashabih): Text that is ambiguous in a way that human reason cannot comprehend, requiring suspension of judgment.
خفی (khafi): A text whose hiddenness is due to a subtle reason but can be uncovered with little thought.
مشکل (mushkil): A text that is problematic and requires reflection (ta'mmul) and ijtihad to resolve its ambiguity.
توقف (tawaqquf): Suspension of judgment, refraining from interpretation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a mutashabih text?
A) Inquiry (talab)
B) Reflection (ta'mmul)
C) Asking for clarification (istifsar)
D) Suspension of judgment (tawaqquf)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul provides a graded response to textual ambiguity: inquiry for khafi, ijtihad for mushkil, clarification for mujmal, and suspension for mutashabih.

Conclusiveness of Linguistic Evidence: Hanafi Response to the Probabilistic Objection
Refuting the claim that all linguistic evidence is only zanni

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi argument that some linguistic evidence is qat'i and evaluate the opposing view that all dalil lafzi is zanni.

Core Idea
Some linguistic facts are mutawatir, making any composition based on them qat'i.

A fundamental debate in Usul al-Fiqh concerns whether linguistic evidence (dalil lafzi) can yield certainty (qat') or only probability (zann). The objectors argue that such evidence depends on fallible transmission and conditions like absence of metaphor, which are known by induction. The Hanafi author counters that some linguistic elements are mutawatir, and compositions from them are certain. This lesson unpacks that argument and the two-tiered concept of conclusive knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing claim and its basis
The objector claims all linguistic evidence is zanni because it depends on ahad transmission for positive conditions and on induction for negative conditions, both yielding only probability.
The objector is the Mutakallimun or some early usulis.
2
Analyze the Hanafi refutation
The author declares the objection false. He points to linguistic facts that are mutawatir: e.g., 'subject is nominative, object is accusative' and 'daraba is past tense'. These are known with certainty.
Tawatur here is about the linguistic custom, not a specific report.
3
Examine the proof: the verse 'إن الله بكل شيء عليم'
Since each word and the grammatical structure are mutawatir, the composition is qat'i. Denying this is like denying the existence of Baghdad, known through mutawatir reports.
This shifts the burden: some compositions are certain, not all.
4
Distinguish the two types of qat'i knowledge
First type: no possibility of contrary meaning at all (in muhkam and mutawatir). Second type: eliminates probability arising from evidence but allows probability without evidence (in zahir, nass, mashhur).
This distinction is critical for Hanafi textual hierarchy.
5
Apply to usul al-fiqh methodology
The Hanafi mujtahid treats zahir texts as qat'i in dalalah for practical purposes, weighting them accordingly in ijtihad.
The practical consequence: verses of ahkam are more firmly binding than if they were merely zanni.

بھی ختم ہو جائینگی . واعلم ان العلماء یعنی علماء حضرات علم قطعی کا اطلاق دو معنی پر کرتے میں احدهما ما يقطع الاحتمال اصلا یعنی جس کے اندر خلاف مراد احتمال بالکل نہ ہو نہ احتمال ناشی بالدلیل اور نہ شی بلا دلیل اس قسم کا علم قطعی محکم اور متواتر میں ہوتا ہے۔ والثانی دوسرا یہ کہ ایسا علم جو احتمال ناشی عن الدلیل کو ختم کر دے اگر چہ احتمال ناشی بلا دلیل اس میں آسکتا ہے یہ بھی علم قطعی کہلاتا ہے ظاهر نص اور خبر مشہور سے یہی علم قطعی حاصل ہوتا ہوں قسم کو علم الیقین کہا جاتا ہے اور ثانی کو علم الطمانينة
The meanings [of words] are known from the rules of grammar, and morphology (sarf) because the forms of individual words are known from morphology, since discussions of forms — this is past tense, this is present, etc. — are in morphology. Knowing the meanings of words depends on the knowledge of forms. These are existential matters, and similarly, it depends on several non-existential matters: no homonymy, no metaphor, no ellipsis (i.e., no implied phrase), no transposition (i.e., the word is not transferred from its original meaning to another), no specification, no forward or backward arrangement. An example given for forward/backward arrangement is the verse "Asra al-nahwi alladhina zalamu" because "alladhina zalamu" cannot be the subject of "asra" since it is a visible noun, and when the subject is a visible noun, the verb cannot be plural; here the verb "asra" is plural, so the implied construction is: "Wa alladhina zalamu asra al-nahwi" such that the relative clause is the subject and "asra" is its predicate. This forward/backward arrangement is done to avoid it being of the type of "akaluni al-baraghithu" where the same issue arises: "al-baraghithu" is a visible noun that is the subject and "akaluni" is plural. That example is interpreted according to a weak dialect: the plural waw in the verb is not a subject pronoun but a marker indicating that its subject will come in plural form, like the ta of femininity in "darabat" indicates that its subject is feminine. This is a weak dialect, and the Qur'anic verse is interpreted with forward/backward arrangement to avoid it being of that weak dialect. Also: no abrogator, no rational objection — meaning the linguistic evidence should have no abrogator and no rational counterargument. The specification of rational is because a transmitted counterargument is subject to interpretation. These essential matters, whether existential or non-existential, are all conditions. As for existential matters, their basis is transmission and narration, and narrators are not infallible, so transmission via ahad cannot be certain, and transmission via tawatur is not in these matters. As for non-existential matters, their basis is induction, and induction only yields probability, not certainty. Therefore, linguistic evidence is probable, not certain. The author responded to this objection by saying: "This is false" — what was said that linguistic evidence does not yield certainty is false, because some languages and grammatical and morphological issues and rules have reached the level of tawatur, like those languages that are extremely famous and well-known, and this grammatical rule that the subject is nominative and the object is accusative, and this morphological rule that "daraba" and words on that pattern are past tense — these have reached tawatur. So every composition composed from such well-known things will certainly be conclusive, like His statement, the Exalted: "Indeed Allah of everything is Knowing." And we do not claim that all transmitted things are certain, but denying that some are certain is obstinacy. Whoever claims that not a single composition is certain is in reality denying all mutawatirat, like denying the existence of Baghdad, because the existence of Baghdad is also known through a declarative composition. In any case, the statement and claim of these deniers is based on sophistry and obstinacy, because it is based on a flimsy argument and fallacy — that is sophistry; otherwise it is obstinacy and denial of the necessary. And rational people do not use [metaphor, ellipsis, etc.] except in non-existential matters? No, these are contrary to the default, and rational people do not use the contrary to the default in their speech in the absence of a contextual indicator, so these probabilities of metaphor, ellipsis, etc. are invalid. Also, sometimes it is known through conclusive contextual indications that the original meaning is intended, otherwise the benefit of addressing would be nullified. If these probabilities were considered valid — perhaps it is metaphor or ellipsis — then no benefit would come from addressing, and such probabilities would even undermine the certainty of mutawatirat. And know that the scholars apply the term "conclusive knowledge" to two meanings: one is that which cuts off probability entirely, i.e., there is no possibility of contrary meaning at all — neither probability arising from evidence nor without evidence; this type of conclusive knowledge occurs in muhkam and mutawatir. The second is knowledge that eliminates probability arising from evidence, even if probability without evidence can enter it; this is also called conclusive knowledge, and it is obtained from zahir, nass, and mashhur reports. The first type is called "ilm al-yaqin" and the second is called "ilm al-tuma'ninah".
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage addresses a fundamental Usul al-Fiqh debate: whether linguistic evidence (dalil lafzi) can produce certainty (qat'i) or only probability (zanni). The objection raised is that such evidence depends on transmission (which is fallible) and on conditions like absence of metaphor, ellipsis, etc., which are negative matters known by induction (which is only probable). Therefore, the objector claims, all linguistic evidence is zanni. The Hanafi author rebuts this by first pointing out that some linguistic facts (e.g., subject is nominative, object is accusative) are mutawatir (conveyed by such widespread transmission that certainty is attained). Consequently, any composition built on these well-known elements is itself qat'i. He gives the Qur'anic verse "Indeed Allah of everything is Knowing" as an example of such a composition. He further argues that denying the certainty of all such compositions is like denying the existence of Baghdad, which is known through reports (khabar) that are effectively mutawatir. The author then refines the concept of 'conclusive knowledge' (ilm qat'i), distinguishing two types: (1) absolute certainty that excludes all possibility of the contrary (found in muhkam and mutawatir texts), and (2) certainty that excludes only probability arising from a textual evidence (but leaves open possibility without evidence), found in zahir, nass, and mashhur. This distinction is crucial for Hanafi usul, where the hierarchical strength of texts (zahir → nass → mufassar → muhkam) determines the level of certainty. The passage defends the Hanafi position that linguistic evidence can indeed yield certainty, against the view of some scholars (likely the Mutakallimun) who held it to be purely zanni.

Key Terms
دلیل لفظی (dalil lafzi): Evidence derived from the wording of a text (Qur'an, Hadith) as opposed to rational evidence.
قطعی (qat'i): Conclusive knowledge that is certain and requires definitive action. Here divided into two types: absolute (لا احتمال أصلاً) and relative (قطع احتمال ناشی عن الدلیل).
ظنی (zanni): Probable knowledge that falls short of certainty; it is still binding in practice but may be outweighed by stronger evidence.
متواتر (mutawatir): A report transmitted by such a large number of narrators that collusion on a falsehood is impossible, yielding certain knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, which of the following is true about linguistic evidence (dalil lafzi)?
A) All linguistic evidence is zanni because it depends on fallible narration.
B) Only the Qur'an is qat'i; other texts are zanni.
C) Some linguistic evidence is qat'i if it is composed of mutawatir linguistic elements.
D) Linguistic evidence is never qat'i due to the possibility of metaphor and ellipsis.

Key Takeaway
Linguistic evidence can be qat'i when it relies on mutawatir linguistic elements, even if its transmission is not mutawatir.

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy

The Two Primary Textual Indications: 'Ibarat al-Nass and Isharat al-Nass
Defines and differentiates 'ibarat and isharat with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between 'ibarat al-nass and isharat al-nass and identify each in Quranic and legal texts.

Core Idea
The direct subject of a text is 'ibarat; its parts and necessary consequences are isharat.

In Hanafi usul, the text (nass) yields more than its literal meaning. Scholars have categorized textual indications to capture both the primary ruling and associated implications. This lesson introduces the two fundamental categories: 'ibarat al-nass, which conveys the subject matter directly, and isharat al-nass, which indicates a part or necessary consequence of that subject matter. Understanding this distinction is essential for deriving rulings from revelation with precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject matter (mawdu' lahu)
Determine the primary meaning that the text is directly about. This is what the scholars call 'ibarat al-nass.
The context (siyaq) is set for this meaning.
2
Identify the parts (juz') and necessary consequences (lazim)
Look for meanings that are either a part of the subject matter or a logical consequence of it. These are indicated by isharat al-nass.
They are established by the textual arrangement (nazm).
3
Apply to the khumus verse example
The verse obligates a share from spoils for the poor ('ibarat). The removal of ownership over left property is a part of the concept of 'poor' (isharat).
4
Apply to the maintenance verse example
The verse obligates a husband to provide for his wife ('ibarat). The father's exclusive responsibility for child maintenance is a necessary consequence (isharat).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ان سے ان کا ملک زائل ہو چکا ہے ۔ معنی اول یعنی ایجاب سهم من الغنیمہ آیت کا موضوع لہ معنی ہے. اور اسی کو علما نے عبارة النص کہا ہے تو یہ معنی موضوع لہ ثابت بالنظم ہے اور معنی ثانی یعنی ان کے ملک کا زوال ان اشیاء سے جو دارالحرب میں چھوڑ آئے. یہ لفظ فقراء کے موضوع لہ کی جز ہے لان الفقراء کیونکہ فقراء وہ لوگ ہوتے ہیں جو کسی شئی کے مالک نہ ہوں اب ان کا صرف ما خلّفوا فی دار الحرب کا مالک نہ ہوتا یہ جز ہے اور ان کا کسی شئی کا مالک نہ ہونا یہ بدرجہ کل ہے ۔ فلما سموا جب انھیں نے دلالت لفظ على زوال ملكهم عما خلّفوا کو اشارۃ النص کہا ہے اور اشارہ وہی ہوتا ہے جو ثابت بالنظم ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر دلالتہ لفظ کو اشارۃ النص کہا جائے گا۔ واما ان اللازم المتأخر ثابت بالنظم اور لازم متاخر یہ بھی ان کی نزدیک ثابت بالنظم ہے فلانهم قالوا ان قوله تعالى وعلى المولود له رزقهن اس لئے کہ انھوں نے کہا ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا یہ قول وعلی المولود لہ سبق لایجاب نفقہ یہ چلایا گیا ہے کہ ان زوجات کا نفقہ زوج پر واجب ہے جنہوں نے ان کا بچہ جنا ہے۔ اور یہ معنی اس کا موضوع اعلہ ہے ۔ وفیہ اشارہ اور اس آیت میں علی المولود لہ کے لفظ سے اشارہ ہے کہ انفاق علی الولد کے بارہ میں باپ منفرد ہے ۔ اذا لا یشارکہ کیونکہ مولود لہ میں جو ولد کی نسبت باپ کی طرف کی گئی ہے۔ اس میں اس کے ساتھ کوئی شریک نہیں ہے۔ فکذاتی حکمھا اسی طرح جو اس نسبتہ کا حکم ہے یعنی اتفاق علی الولد اس میں بھی اس کے ساتھ کوئی شریک نہیں ہو گا - وهذا المعنی یعنی باپ کا منفرد فی النفقہ ہونا یہ موضوع لہ کا لازم خارجی ہے کیونکہ زوجہ کی تخصیص بالزوج اور اس کے لئے محل حرث ہونا اس کا لازم خارجی ہے۔ اختصاص الولد بالاب اور ہے بھی متاخر کیوں کہ بچہ پیدا ہونے کے بعد اختصاص ہوتا ہے۔ ولما جعلوہ جب علما نے اس معنی کی طرف اس آیت میں اشارہ تسلیم کیا ہے تو لازم خارجی جو متاثر ہے تو اس کو ثابت بالنظم تسلیم کیا حاصل یہ کہ تینوں معانی یعنی موضوع له . جز موضوع له - لازم متأخر للموضوع لہ ثابت بالنظم ہیں ۔ فالمثال الاول يعني للفقراء الى آخره في الموضوع له اس کا معنی موضوع لہ ہے ایجاب سهم من الغنيمة اس میں وہ عبارۃ النص ہے ۔ واشارة الى جزئه جز موضوع لہ سے مراد زوال ملکهم بما خلفوا فی دار الحرب ہے اس کے لئے اشارۃ النص ہے ۔ المثال الثانی اس سے مراد وعلی المولود لہ رزقھن ہے۔ عبارة في الموضوع له موضوع لہ اس کا ایجاب نفقة الزوجات ہے اس میں عبارۃ النص ہے ۔ اشارۃ الی لازمہ اور اس کا لازم یعنی انفراد الاب بنفقة الاولاد کے اثبات کے لئے اشارۃ النص ہے وايضا الى جزئه اور جز موضوع لہ یعنی یہ کہ نسب اباء کی جانب ہوتا ہے اس کے لئے بھی یہ آیتہ اشارہ النص ہے ۔ الى آخر ما ذكرنا فی المتن اس کی تفصیل متن میں آرہی ہے ۔ واذا قالت المرأة لزوجها جب عورت اپنے خاوند سے کہتی ہے کہ تو نے میرے اوپر ایک عورت کو نکاح کر لیا ہے فطلقها اس کو طلاق دے دے ۔ فقال ارضاءً كھا خاوند اپنی اس عورت کو راضی کرنے کی خاطر کہتا ہے كل امرأة لی طلاق میری ہر عورت کو طلاق ہے طلقت كلهن قضاءً تمام عورتیں حتی کہ یہ بھی جس کو راضی کر رہا تھا مطلقہ ہو جائینگی قضاءً ۔ قاضی اس کی اس بارہ میں تصدیق نہیں کرے گا کہ مخاطبہ ان میں داخل نہیں تھی فالمعنى الموضوع له اس کلام کا موضوع لہ معنی طلاق جميع نساء لیکن سوق کلام اس کے لئے نہیں ہے وقد سبق الکلام اور اس کلام کا سوق جز موضوع لہ کے لئے ہے وھو طلاق بعض من اور وہ جزء طلاق بعض ہے اس عورت مخاطبہ کے سوا نیکون پس یہ کلام جز موضوع لہ کے لئے عبارة النص ہوگی کیونکہ سوق کلام اسی کی خاطر ہے ۔ واشارة الى الموضوع له موضوع لہ یعنی طلاق کل کے لئے اشارۃ النص ہوگی کیونکہ اس کے لئے سوق کلام نہیں ہے ۔ وايضا اشارة الى الجزء الآخر اور دوسری جز یعنی اسی عورت مخاطبہ کی طلاق میں بھی یہ اشارۃ النص ہوگی کیونکہ سیاق کلام اس کی خاطر نہیں ہے و ایضا الی لازام الموضوع له اور لازم موضوع لہ کیلئے بھی اشارة النص ہوگی وہ لوازم طلاق یعنی وجوب مہر اور وجوب عدة وغیرہ کے لئے اشارۃ النص ہوگی وقوله تعالى واحل الله البيع وحرم الربوا المسبق للامم المتأخر اس آیت کا سوق لازم متآخر کے لئے ہے یعنی تفرقہ بین البیع والربوا اس کے لئے یہ عبارۃ النص ہوگی۔ اور یہ آیت اشارۃ النص ہوگی موضوع لہ کے لئے یعنی حرمتہ رہوا اور حلہ بیع کے لئے اور اس کے اجزاء مثلا حرمته بيع النقدين متفاضل الجنسہ اور لوازم مثلا انتقال ملک فی البیع اور وجوب تسلیم المبیع اور حرمۃ الانتفاع في الربوا ان تمام کے لئے اشارۃ النص ہوگی کیونکہ ان کے لئے سوق کلام نہیں ہے ۔ وانما قيدنا اللازم بالمتأخر الخ دلالۃ النص میں ہم نے لازم کے ساتھ متأخر ہونیکی قید لگادی ہے اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ لانهم سموا دلالة اللفظ على اللازم المتقدم كه علما نے لازم متقدم پر دلالت لفظ کو اقتصاء النص کے ساتھ موسوم کیا انما جعلوا كذلك ایسے کیوں کیا اصل وجہ یہ ہے کہ دلالۃ النص کا درجہ اقتضاء النص سے قومی ہے اس لئے مصنف نے ثابت کیا کہ لازم متاآخر پر دلالہ لفظ قوی ہوتی ہے بنسبت لازم متقدم کے تو کہا لان دلالة الملزوم کیونکہ ملزوم کی دلالہ لازم متأخر پر ایسے ہے جیسے دلالہ علیہ علی المعلول ہوتی ہے اقوی یہ قومی ہے بنسبت دلالہ ملزوم کے جو ایسے لازم پر ہو جو غیر متأخر ہے کیونکہ یہ ایسے ہے جیسے دلالت معلول علی العلہ ہو خان الدولية مطورة دون الثانية کیونکہ دلالۃ اولی یعنی دلالتہ حلته على المعلول مطرد اور کلی ہے یعنی ہر وقت ہے کسی
Their ownership has ceased. The first meaning, i.e., the obligation of a share from the spoils, is the subject matter (mawdu' lahu) of the verse. And the scholars have called this 'ibarat al-nass. So this meaning is established by the text (nass). The second meaning, i.e., the removal of their ownership over the things they left behind in dar al-harb, is a part of the subject matter of the word 'fugara', because 'fugara' are those who own nothing. Now they are not owners only of what they left in dar al-harb; this is a part. And their not owning anything is the whole. So when they [the scholars] called the indication of the word over the removal of their ownership over what they left as isharat al-nass, and isharah is that which is established by the text. Therefore, the indication of the word over this will be called isharat al-nass. As for the delayed necessary consequence (lazim muta'akhkhir), it is also established by the text in their view, because they said that the statement of Allah 'And upon the father their provision' is used to establish the obligation of maintenance for the wives who bore his child. And this meaning is the subject matter. And in it is an indication: from the phrase 'upon the father' there is an indication that the father is solely responsible for the child's maintenance, for there is no partner with him. Because in 'mawlud lahu' the child is attributed to the father alone, so the ruling is likewise: he alone is responsible for the child's maintenance. And this meaning, i.e., the father's exclusivity in maintenance, is an external necessary consequence of the subject matter, because the wife's specification to the husband and her being a place of cultivation is its external necessary consequence. The child's exclusive attribution to the father is also later, because the attribution occurs after the child's birth. When the scholars accepted that there is an indication to this meaning in the verse, then the external necessary consequence that is later is accepted as established by the text. The gist: all three meanings—subject matter, part of subject matter, delayed necessary consequence of subject matter—are established by the text. The first example: the meaning for the poor etc. in the subject matter: the obligation of a share from spoils—this is 'ibarat al-nass. And the indication to its part: the removal of their ownership over what they left in dar al-harb—this is isharat al-nass. The second example: from 'And upon the father their provision'—the subject matter is the obligation of maintenance for wives, this is 'ibarat al-nass. The indication to its necessary consequence: the father's exclusivity in maintenance of children is isharat al-nass, and also to its part: that lineage is to the father—this verse also indicates that. Details are coming in the text. And if a woman says to her husband, 'You have married another woman over me, so divorce her,' and the husband, to please her, says, 'Every woman of mine is divorced,' then all women are divorced judicially, including the one he was trying to please. The judge will not accept his claim that the addressed woman was not included. The subject matter of this speech is the meaning of divorce of all women, but the context (siyaq) is not for that; the context is for a part of the subject matter, i.e., divorce of some, specifically the addressed woman. Thus this speech is 'ibarat al-nass for the part, because the context is for it. And it is isharat al-nass for the subject matter (divorce of all), because the context is not for it. And also isharat al-nass for the other part (the addressed woman's divorce), because the context is not for it, and also for the necessary consequences of the subject matter, like the obligation of dower and 'iddah—these are isharat al-nass. And His statement, 'And Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury'—the context of this verse is for a delayed necessary consequence, i.e., the distinction between trade and usury; this is 'ibarat al-nass. And this verse is isharat al-nass for the subject matter, i.e., the prohibition of usury and permissibility of trade, and for its parts, e.g., the prohibition of exchanging disparate amounts of the same genus, and for its necessary consequences, like the transfer of ownership in trade and the obligation to deliver the sold item and the prohibition of using usury—all these are isharat al-nass because the context is not for them. And we restricted the necessary consequence to the delayed one: the reason is that the scholars termed the indication of the word over a prior necessary consequence (lazim mutaqaddim) as iqtida' al-nass. They did so because the rank of dalaalat al-nass is stronger than iqtida' al-nass. So the author established that the indication of the word over a delayed necessary consequence is stronger than over a prior necessary consequence. He said: 'Because the indication of the necessary condition (malzum) over the delayed necessary consequence is like the indication of a cause over an effect—it is stronger' relative to the indication of the malzum over a non-delayed necessary consequence, which is like the indication of an effect over a cause. The first indication is universal and general, i.e., it occurs always.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih clarifies the classification of textual indications in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author distinguishes between 'ibarat al-nass (direct expression), isharat al-nass (indication), and then later introduces dalaalat al-nass and iqtida' al-nass. The key point is that the subject matter (mawdu' lahu) of a text, i.e., the primary ruling intended, is expressed through 'ibarat al-nass. However, associated meanings—such as a part of that subject matter (juz') or a necessary consequence (lazim) that follows from it—are indicated by isharat al-nass, provided they are established by the arrangement of the text (nass). The author gives multiple examples: (1) The khumus verse: the obligation of giving a share from spoils is 'ibarat al-nass; the removal of fighters' ownership over left-behind property is a part (since the poor who receive cannot own it), thus isharat al-nass. (2) The verse on maintenance: the obligation for a husband to provide for his wife is 'ibarat al-nass; the father's exclusive responsibility for child support and the attribution of lineage to him are necessary consequences and parts, thus isharat al-nass. (3) A husband's statement 'every woman of mine is divorced': the context shows his intent to divorce only one wife, so that wife's divorce is 'ibarat al-nass (since the context is for it), but the divorce of all women, the other wives, and the necessary consequences (dower, 'iddah) are isharat al-nass. (4) The verse on trade and usury: the context emphasizes the distinction (lazim muta'akhkhir), so it is 'ibarat al-nass for that distinction, but the rulings themselves (permissibility of trade, prohibition of usury) are isharat al-nass. Finally, the author explains why the lazim muta'akhkhir is given a special name (dalaalat al-nass): because its indication is stronger, like a cause indicating its effect universally, whereas a prior necessary consequence (lazim mutaqaddim) is indicated by iqtida' al-nass, which is weaker, like an effect indicating its cause (not always present). This distinction helps jurists prioritize proofs when deriving rulings.

Key Terms
عبارة النص (‘Ibarat al-Nass): The direct meaning of the text that is the subject matter and for which the context is set.
إشارة النص (Isharat al-Nass): Indication of the text to a meaning that is a part of the subject matter or a necessary consequence of it, not directly intended by the context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi usul, what type of textual indication covers a part (juz') of the subject matter?
A) 'Ibarat al-nass
B) Isharat al-nass
C) Dalaalat al-nass
D) Iqtida' al-nass

Key Takeaway
A single Qur'anic text can yield multiple rulings: the direct subject (ibarat) and its parts/consequences (isharat) – both are established by the textual arrangement.

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy
advanced
10 min
Subtypes of Isharat: Dalalat al-Nass and Iqtida' al-Nass
Extends isharat to subtypes: dalalat al-nass and iqtida' al-nass with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between dalalat al-nass (indication to a delayed necessary consequence) and iqtida' al-nass (indication to a prior necessary consequence) and apply the strength hierarchy.

Core Idea
Delayed necessary consequences (lazim muta'akhkhir) are stronger than prior ones (lazim mutaqaddim) because they are like cause indicating effect.

In the previous lesson, we learned that isharat al-nass covers parts and necessary consequences. The Hanafi scholars further divide these necessary consequences into two types: those that come after the subject matter (dalalat al-nass) and those that are presupposed (iqtida' al-nass). This distinction affects the strength of the indication and is crucial in resolving apparent conflicts between textual implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject matter (mawdu' lahu)
Start with the primary meaning of the text – its 'ibarat al-nass.
2
Determine if a necessary consequence is delayed (lazim muta'akhkhir) or prior (lazim mutaqaddim)
A delayed consequence occurs after the subject matter, e.g., exclusivity of father in maintenance after birth. A prior consequence must be assumed for the text to make sense, e.g., that a husband exists for the verse on maintenance.
Delayed consequences are indicated by dalalat al-nass, prior by iqtida' al-nass.
3
Apply to the examples: husband's statement 'every woman of mine is divorced' and the trade/usury verse
In the husband's statement, the context shows he intends divorce of one wife, so that is 'ibarat; the divorce of all is isharat (subject matter). The necessary consequences like dower and 'iddah are also isharat but are delayed. In the trade/usury verse, the distinction between them is the delayed consequence (dalalat al-nass), while the rulings themselves are isharat.
4
Understand the strength hierarchy: dalalat al-nass > iqtida' al-nass
Because dalalat al-nass is like a cause indicating its effect (always present), while iqtida' al-nass is like an effect indicating a cause (not always present).
This helps in tarjih when proofs conflict.

ان سے ان کا ملک زائل ہو چکا ہے ۔ معنی اول یعنی ایجاب سهم من الغنیمہ آیت کا موضوع لہ معنی ہے. اور اسی کو علما نے عبارة النص کہا ہے تو یہ معنی موضوع لہ ثابت بالنظم ہے اور معنی ثانی یعنی ان کے ملک کا زوال ان اشیاء سے جو دارالحرب میں چھوڑ آئے. یہ لفظ فقراء کے موضوع لہ کی جز ہے لان الفقراء کیونکہ فقراء وہ لوگ ہوتے ہیں جو کسی شئی کے مالک نہ ہوں اب ان کا صرف ما خلّفوا فی دار الحرب کا مالک نہ ہوتا یہ دلالتہ لفظ کو اشارۃ النص کہا جائے گا۔ واما ان اللازم المتأخر ثابت بالنظم اور لازم متاخر یہ بھی ان کی نزدیک ثابت بالنظم ہے فلانهم قالوا ان قوله تعالى وعلى المولود له رزقهن اس لئے کہ انھوں نے کہا ہے کہ خارجی جو متاثر ہے تو اس کو ثابت بالنظم تسلیم کیا حاصل یہ کہ تینوں معانی یعنی موضوع له . جز موضوع له - لازم متأخر للموضوع لہ ثابت بالنظم ہیں ۔ فالمثال الاول يعني للفقراء الى آخره في الموضوع له اس کا لہ رزقھن ہے۔ عبارة في الموضوع له موضوع لہ اس کا ایجاب نفقة الزوجات ہے اس میں عبارۃ النص ہے ۔ اشارۃ الی لازمہ اور اس کا لازم یعنی انفراد الاب بنفقة الاولاد کے اثبات کے لئے اشارۃ النص ہے وايضا الى جزئه اور جز موضوع لہ یعنی یہ کہ نسب اباء کی جانب ہوتا ہے اس کے لئے بھی یہ آیتہ اشارہ النص ہے ۔ الى آخر ما ذكرنا فی المتن اس کی تفصیل متن میں آرہی ہے ۔ واذا قالت المرأة لزوجها جب عورت اپنے خاوند سے کہتی ہے کہ تو نے میرے اوپر ایک عورت کو نکاح کر لیا ہے فطلقها اس کو طلاق دے دے ۔ فقال ارضاءً كھا خاوند اپنی اس عورت کو راضی کرنے کی خاطر کہتا ہے كل امرأة لی طلاق میری ہر عورت کو طلاق ہے طلقت كلهن قضاءً تمام عورتیں حتی کہ یہ بھی جس کو راضی کر رہا تھا مطلقہ ہو جائینگی قضاءً ۔ قاضی اس کی اس بارہ میں تصدیق نہیں کرے گا کہ مخاطبہ ان میں داخل نہیں تھی فالمعنى الموضوع له اس کلام کا موضوع لہ معنی طلاق جميع نساء لیکن سوق کلام اس کے لئے نہیں ہے وقد سبق الکلام اور اس کلام کا سوق جز موضوع لہ کے لئے ہے وھو طلاق بعض من اور وہ جزء طلاق بعض ہے اس عورت مخاطبہ کے سوا نیکون پس یہ کلام جز موضوع لہ کے لئے عبارة النص ہوگی کیونکہ سوق کلام اسی کی خاطر ہے ۔ واشارة الى الموضوع له موضوع لہ یعنی طلاق کل کے لئے اشارۃ النص ہوگی کیونکہ اس کے لئے سوق کلام نہیں ہے ۔ وايضا اشارة الى الجزء الآخر اور دوسری جز یعنی اسی عورت مخاطبہ کی طلاق میں بھی یہ اشارۃ النص ہوگی کیونکہ سیاق کلام اس کی خاطر نہیں ہے و ایضا الی لازام الموضوع له اور لازم موضوع لہ کیلئے بھی اشارة النص ہوگی وہ لوازم طلاق یعنی وجوب مہر اور وجوب عدة وغیرہ کے لئے اشارۃ النص ہوگی وقوله تعالى واحل الله البيع وحرم الربوا المسبق للامم المتأخر اس آیت کا سوق لازم متآخر کے لئے ہے یعنی تفرقہ بین البیع والربوا اس کے لئے یہ عبارۃ النص ہوگی۔ اور یہ آیت اشارۃ النص ہوگی موضوع لہ کے لئے یعنی حرمتہ رہوا اور حلہ بیع کے لئے اور اس کے اجزاء مثلا حرمته بيع النقدين متفاضل الجنسہ اور لوازم مثلا انتقال ملک فی البیع اور وجوب تسلیم المبیع اور حرمۃ الانتفاع في الربوا ان تمام کے لئے اشارۃ النص ہوگی کیونکہ ان کے لئے سوق کلام نہیں ہے ۔ وانما قيدنا اللازم بالمتأخر الخ دلالۃ النص میں ہم نے لازم کے ساتھ متأخر ہونیکی قید لگادی ہے اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ لانهم سموا دلالة اللفظ على اللازم المتقدم كه علما نے لازم متقدم پر دلالت لفظ کو اقتصاء النص کے ساتھ موسوم کیا انما جعلوا كذلك ایسے کیوں کیا اصل وجہ یہ ہے کہ دلالۃ النص کا درجہ اقتضاء النص سے قومی ہے اس لئے مصنف نے ثابت کیا کہ لازم متاآخر پر دلالہ لفظ قوی ہوتی ہے بنسبت لازم متقدم کے تو کہا لان دلالة الملزوم کیونکہ ملزوم کی دلالہ لازم متأخر پر ایسے ہے جیسے دلالہ علیہ علی المعلول ہوتی ہے اقوی یہ قومی ہے بنسبت دلالہ ملزوم کے جو ایسے لازم پر ہو جو غیر متأخر ہے کیونکہ یہ ایسے ہے جیسے دلالت معلول علی العلہ ہو خان الدولية مطورة دون الثانية کیونکہ دلالۃ اولی یعنی دلالتہ حلته على المعلول مطرد اور کلی ہے یعنی ہر وقت ہے کسی
Their ownership has ceased. The first meaning, i.e., the obligation of a share from the spoils, is the subject matter (mawdu' lahu) of the verse. And the scholars have called this 'ibarat al-nass. So this meaning is established by the text (nass). The second meaning, i.e., the removal of their ownership over the things they left behind in dar al-harb, is a part of the subject matter of the word 'fugara', because 'fugara' are those who own nothing. Now they are not owners only of what they left in dar al-harb; this is a part. And their not owning anything is the whole. So when they [the scholars] called the indication of the word over the removal of their ownership over what they left as isharat al-nass, and isharah is that which is established by the text. Therefore, the indication of the word over this will be called isharat al-nass. As for the delayed necessary consequence (lazim muta'akhkhir), it is also established by the text in their view, because they said that the statement of Allah 'And upon the father their provision' is used to establish the obligation of maintenance for the wives who bore his child. And this meaning is the subject matter. And in it is an indication: from the phrase 'upon the father' there is an indication that the father is solely responsible for the child's maintenance, for there is no partner with him. Because in 'mawlud lahu' the child is attributed to the father alone, so the ruling is likewise: he alone is responsible for the child's maintenance. And this meaning, i.e., the father's exclusivity in maintenance, is an external necessary consequence of the subject matter, because the wife's specification to the husband and her being a place of cultivation is its external necessary consequence. The child's exclusive attribution to the father is also later, because the attribution occurs after the child's birth. When the scholars accepted that there is an indication to this meaning in the verse, then the external necessary consequence that is later is accepted as established by the text. The gist: all three meanings—subject matter, part of subject matter, delayed necessary consequence of subject matter—are established by the text. The first example: the meaning for the poor etc. in the subject matter: the obligation of a share from spoils—this is 'ibarat al-nass. And the indication to its part: the removal of their ownership over what they left in dar al-harb—this is isharat al-nass. The second example: from 'And upon the father their provision'—the subject matter is the obligation of maintenance for wives, this is 'ibarat al-nass. The indication to its necessary consequence: the father's exclusivity in maintenance of children is isharat al-nass, and also to its part: that lineage is to the father—this verse also indicates that. Details are coming in the text. And if a woman says to her husband, 'You have married another woman over me, so divorce her,' and the husband, to please her, says, 'Every woman of mine is divorced,' then all women are divorced judicially, including the one he was trying to please. The judge will not accept his claim that the addressed woman was not included. The subject matter of this speech is the meaning of divorce of all women, but the context (siyaq) is not for that; the context is for a part of the subject matter, i.e., divorce of some, specifically the addressed woman. Thus this speech is 'ibarat al-nass for the part, because the context is for it. And it is isharat al-nass for the subject matter (divorce of all), because the context is not for it. And also isharat al-nass for the other part (the addressed woman's divorce), because the context is not for it, and also for the necessary consequences of the subject matter, like the obligation of dower and 'iddah—these are isharat al-nass. And His statement, 'And Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury'—the context of this verse is for a delayed necessary consequence, i.e., the distinction between trade and usury; this is 'ibarat al-nass. And this verse is isharat al-nass for the subject matter, i.e., the prohibition of usury and permissibility of trade, and for its parts, e.g., the prohibition of exchanging disparate amounts of the same genus, and for its necessary consequences, like the transfer of ownership in trade and the obligation to deliver the sold item and the prohibition of using usury—all these are isharat al-nass because the context is not for them. And we restricted the necessary consequence to the delayed one: the reason is that the scholars termed the indication of the word over a prior necessary consequence (lazim mutaqaddim) as iqtida' al-nass. They did so because the rank of dalaalat al-nass is stronger than iqtida' al-nass. So the author established that the indication of the word over a delayed necessary consequence is stronger than over a prior necessary consequence. He said: 'Because the indication of the necessary condition (malzum) over the delayed necessary consequence is like the indication of a cause over an effect—it is stronger' relative to the indication of the malzum over a non-delayed necessary consequence, which is like the indication of an effect over a cause. The first indication is universal and general, i.e., it occurs always.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih clarifies the classification of textual indications in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author distinguishes between 'ibarat al-nass (direct expression), isharat al-nass (indication), and then later introduces dalaalat al-nass and iqtida' al-nass. The key point is that the subject matter (mawdu' lahu) of a text, i.e., the primary ruling intended, is expressed through 'ibarat al-nass. However, associated meanings—such as a part of that subject matter (juz') or a necessary consequence (lazim) that follows from it—are indicated by isharat al-nass, provided they are established by the arrangement of the text (nass). The author gives multiple examples: (1) The khumus verse: the obligation of giving a share from spoils is 'ibarat al-nass; the removal of fighters' ownership over left-behind property is a part (since the poor who receive cannot own it), thus isharat al-nass. (2) The verse on maintenance: the obligation for a husband to provide for his wife is 'ibarat al-nass; the father's exclusive responsibility for child support and the attribution of lineage to him are necessary consequences and parts, thus isharat al-nass. (3) A husband's statement 'every woman of mine is divorced': the context shows his intent to divorce only one wife, so that wife's divorce is 'ibarat al-nass (since the context is for it), but the divorce of all women, the other wives, and the necessary consequences (dower, 'iddah) are isharat al-nass. (4) The verse on trade and usury: the context emphasizes the distinction (lazim muta'akhkhir), so it is 'ibarat al-nass for that distinction, but the rulings themselves (permissibility of trade, prohibition of usury) are isharat al-nass. Finally, the author explains why the lazim muta'akhkhir is given a special name (dalaalat al-nass): because its indication is stronger, like a cause indicating its effect universally, whereas a prior necessary consequence (lazim mutaqaddim) is indicated by iqtida' al-nass, which is weaker, like an effect indicating its cause (not always present). This distinction helps jurists prioritize proofs when deriving rulings.

Key Terms
دلالة النص (Dalalat al-Nass): Indication of the text to a delayed necessary consequence (lazim muta'akhkhir), considered stronger.
اقتضاء النص (Iqtida' al-Nass): Indication of the text to a prior necessary consequence (lazim mutaqaddim), considered weaker.
لازم متأخر (Lazim muta'akhkhir): A necessary consequence that comes after the subject matter in time or logical order.
لازم متقدم (Lazim mutaqaddim): A necessary consequence that must precede the subject matter for the text to be coherent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of textual indication is stronger according to the Hanafi hierarchy described in the passage?
A) 'Ibarat al-nass
B) Isharat al-nass
C) Dalaalat al-nass
D) Iqtida' al-nass

Key Takeaway
Within isharat al-nass, delayed necessary consequences (dalalat) are given more weight than prior ones (iqtida') due to the cause-effect relationship.

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy
advanced
12 min
The Four Types of Textual Indications in Hanafi Usul
Defining and distinguishing four types of textual indications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define and distinguish the four types of textual indications in Hanafi usul, apply them to Quranic examples, and explain why dalalat al-nass is considered stronger than qiyas.

Core Idea
A text indicates its ruling through four pathways: explicit wording, part of the meaning, necessary prior, or a universally understood cause.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih presents the Hanafi classification of textual indications. Understanding these four types is essential for deriving rulings directly from the Quran and Sunnah. The author also clarifies a critical distinction: dalalat al-nass is a direct textual indication recognized by any Arabic speaker, unlike qiyas which requires ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Types
List the four types of textual indications: 'ibarah al-nass (explicit wording), isharah al-nass (implied part), iqtida' al-nass (necessary prior condition), and dalalat al-nass (indication via a self-evident cause). Understand their definitions from the passage.
'Ibarah is the direct ruling intended by the context; isharah is a secondary implication; iqtida' is a logical requirement for the text to be valid; dalalah is based on a cause understood by all language experts.
2
Understand the Logical Distinction
The passage explains that indication from cause to effect is constant (muttarid), but from effect to cause is not. This grounds the hierarchy: texts that establish the cause are stronger than those that establish the effect.
Example: sunrise (cause) always indicates light (effect), but light does not always indicate sunrise.
3
Apply the Definitions to Quranic Examples
Analyze the examples given: the verse about poor emigrants (59:8) is 'ibarah for their entitlement to booty and isharah for loss of ownership. The verse about foster mothers (2:233) is 'ibarah for the father's obligation and isharah for lineage and guardianship.
Also note the key example: 'Do not say to them 'uff'' (17:23) used for dalalat al-nass to prohibit hitting.
4
Distinguish Dalalat al-Nass from Qiyas
The author argues that dalalat al-nass relies on a cause that every language expert understands, whereas qiyas requires a mujtahid to identify the cause. Therefore, dalalat al-nass is a stronger proof and is included among the four types, while qiyas is excluded.
This is a unique Hanafi contribution; other schools may treat such derivations as qiyas jali (obvious analogy).

مخصوص وقت اور شرط کے ساتھ وابستہ نہیں ہے اور ثانیہ یعنی دلالتہ معلول علی العلة مطرد نہیں ہے اذ لا دلالة للمعلول على العلة کیونکہ معلول کی دلالۃ علی العلہ صرف اس وقت ہوتی ہے جب معلول مساوی للعلہ ہو اگر مساواہ نہ ہو تو دلالتہ یقینی نہیں ہو سکتی دیکھتے طلوع شمس علتہ برائے وجود ضوء ہے جب طلوع شمس کا علم ہو گا تو اس کے ساتھ علم بالضوء ضرور ثابت ہو گا عکس نہیں ہے یعنی نبوت ضور سے طلوع شمس کا ثبوت ضروری نہیں ہے ہو سکتا ہے کہ یہ ضوء من النار ہو تو جب دلالۃ اولی مطرد ہوئی تو وہ قومی من الثانیہ ہو گی جو غیر مطرد ہے ۔ دلان النص یہ دلالۃ اولی کے اقومی ہونے کی دوسری دلیل ہے حاصل یہ کہ جو نص مثبت للعلہ ہوتی ہے وہ ضرور مثبت للمحلول ہوتی ہے تبعاً کیونکہ معلول تابع ہے اور عملہ درجہ اصل میں ہے جب اصل ثابت ہوا تو تابع ضرور ثابت ہوگا ۔ اما المثبت للمعلول جو مثبت معلول ہو وہ مثبت للعلہ جو کہ اصل ہے بنسبت معلول کے قرار نہیں دی جا سکتی خلاصہ یہ کہ جو مثبت تابع ہو اس کو مثبت متبوع قرار نہیں دیا جاتا۔ فیحسن ان یقال پس مستحسن یہی ہے کہ کہا جائے کہ معلول ثابت ہے عبارة النص کے ساتھ جو علتہ کو ثابت کرتی ہے۔ ولا يحسن ان یقال اور نہ مستحسن نہیں ہے کہ کہا جائے کہ علہ ثابت ہے اس عبارۃ النص کے ساتھ جو مثبت معلول ہے۔ فتبين من هذه ان السجات مذکورہ سے عبارة النص اور اشارۃ النص اور اقتضاء النص کی تعریفات واضح ہو چکی ہیں واما حد دلالة النص اور دلالتہ النص کی تعریف وہی جو مذکور ہوئی ہے اس قول مصنف کے ساتھ علی الحکم فی شئی یعنی لفظ دلالہ کرے اوپر حکم کے ایسی کشتی میں جس کے اندر وہ معنی موجود ہے جو ہر لغت دان سمجھتا ہے کہ منطوق میں یہ حکم اسی معنی کی وجہ سے ہے۔ تو اسی دلالۃ لفظ کو دلالۃ النص کہا جاتا ہے ۔ نحو لا تقل لهما أن یب هذا نظم حرمه ضرب پر دال بدلاله النص ہے کیونکہ ضرب ابوین ایک ایسی شئی ہے کہ اس کے اندر از منی یعنی اینزام ابوین موجود ہے ۔ والاذی معنی اور ازلی ایسا معنی اور سبب ہے کہ ہر عارف لغتہ سمجھتا ہے کہ حکم فی المنطوق یعنی حرمتہ في المنطوق اور منطوق تافیت کہ اس کی حرمتة لاجلہ اسی معنی اذی کیوجہ سے ہے تو دلالہ علی حرمة الصفر دلالة النص ہوئی وجه الحصرتي هذه الدريع ان اربع اقسام میں وجہ حصہ یہ ہے کہ المعنی یعنی معنی جو مراد من السلام ہے اگر عین موضوع لہ ہے یا جن موضوع لہ یا موضوع کا لازم ہے جو اس سے متقدم نہیں تو ان کے لئے وہ لفظ عمارہ النص ہوگا ان سبق الكلام له بشر طیکہ سیاق کلام اسی معنی کی خاطر ہو. واشارة النص ان توثیق اور اشارۃ النص ہو گا اگر اس معنی کے لئے سوق کلام نہ ہو۔ نہ وان كان لازمه المتقدم اگر دلالت لفظ لازم موضوع لہ پر ہو ایسا لازم جو متقدم از معنی موضوعاله فاقتضاء تو یہ اقتضاء النص ہے۔ واللہ لیکن شئ من ذلك اگر ان میں سے کوئی شئی نہ ہو یعنی معنی مرادی نہ عین موضوع لہ ہو نہ جزر موضوع له نه لازم متأخر اور نہ لازم متقدم فان وجد في هذا المعنى اگر اس معنی مرادی میں وہ علہ موجود ہو جو ہر عارف لغتہ سمجھتا ہے کہ منطوق میں حکم اسی علہ کی خاطر ہے تو ایسے معنی مرادی کے لئے دلالہ لفظ دلالۃ النص ہو گی ۔ وان لم یوجد اگر اس قسم کی علہ موجود نہ ہو تو پھر تو کسی قسم کی نہ دلالتہ ہو سکتی اور نہ استدلال ہوسکتا ہے وانما قلنا يفهم كل من يعرف اللغة ہم نے جو یہ کی. کہا کہ اس معنی کو جو منطوق میں علیہ حکم ہے ہر عارف لغتہ سمجھ سکے اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اگر اس معنی اور علیہ کو کوئی نہیں سمجھتا یا بعض سمجھتے ہیں اور بعض نہیں سمجھتے تو فلا دلالت پھر بھی کسی قسم کی دلالہ نہیں ہو گی۔ کیونکہ دلالہ لفظیہ کا اعتبار ہر اس شخص کی بنسبت ہوتا ہے جو عالم بالوضع ہو اور اسی قید کے ساتھ قیاس اقسام دلالہ سے خارج ہو جائیگا فان المعنی فی القیاس کیونکہ جو معنی علہ بنتا ہے قیاس میں اس کو ہر عالم لغتہ نہیں سمجھ سکتا بلکہ اس کو صرف مجتھد سمجھتا ہے . هذا هو یہ ایک انتہائی اقدام تحقیق و تنقیح ہے اس مقام میں جو مصنف نے پیش کیا اور وجوہ دلالت سے اس حد تک کشف عطامہ کرنا یہ مصنف کا حصہ ہے اس سے پہلے کسی نے سبقت نہیں کی اگر اعتماد نہ آئے تو کتب متقدمین متاخرین کا مطالعہ کر کے تجربہ کر دیکھو والله در المصنف رحمه الله تعالی واللہ تعالٰی الموفق كقوله تعالى للفقراء المهاجرین اس آیت کا سوق وسیاق چونکہ اس کے لئے ہے کہ مهاجرين سهم من الغنیہ کا استحقاق رکھتے ہیں اور یہ سھم ان کے لئے واجب و ثابت ہے تو انس اور توار استحقاق و ایجاب کے لئے یہ عبارة النص ہے فیه اشار اور اس میں اس طرف اشارہ ہے جو کچھ دیار و اموال دار الحرب میں چھوڑ آتے ہیں اس سے ان کا ملک زائل ہو چکا ہے کیونکہ فقراء انھیں کہتے ہیں جو کسی شئی کے مالک نہ ہوں لیکن اس کے لئے سوق آیتہ نہیں ہے اگر چہ یہ جز موضوع الہ ہے اس لئے اشارۃ النص ہوگی ۔ وعلى المولود له رزقهن وكسوتھن سبق اس آیتہ کا سیاق اس کے لئے ہے کہ مرضعہ کا نفقہ رضیع کے والد پر واجب ہے اس کے لئے یہ عبارۃ النص ہوگی اور باقی مسائل جو اس آیت سے ثابت ہوتے چونکہ ان کے لئے سوق نظم نہیں لہذا ان تمام مسائل کے اثبات کے لئے اشارة النص ہوگی مثلا یہ مسئلہ کہ نسب الی الاباء ہوتا ہے اور یہ مسئله که ان اللاب ولاية تملك ماله باپ کو یہ ولایتہ اور اختیار حاصل ہے کہ حسب ضرورۃ اپنے دلد کے مال کا مالک بن سکتا ہے لانے الى الولد نسب اليه الى الاب بلام الملك في قوله تعالى المولود له فيقتضی پس یہ نسبت ما
It is not tied to a specific time and condition. And the second, meaning the indication of the effect on the cause, is not constant, because there is no indication from the effect to the cause, since the effect's indication of the cause only occurs when the effect is equal to the cause. If there is no equality, its indication cannot be certain. Observe: the rising of the sun is a cause for the existence of light. When one knows the rising of the sun, knowledge of light is necessarily established, but not vice versa, meaning that from light the rising of the sun is not necessarily proven, as it could be light from fire. So when the first indication is constant, it is stronger than the second, which is not constant. The indication of the text (dalalat al-nass) is the second proof of the superiority of the first indication. The summary is that a text which establishes the cause necessarily establishes the effect as a consequence, because the effect is dependent and the cause is in the degree of the origin. When the origin is established, the dependent is necessarily established. As for that which establishes the effect, which is an establisher of the effect, it cannot be considered an establisher of the cause, which is the origin relative to the effect. In summary, that which establishes the dependent cannot be considered an establisher of the independent. So it is good to say that the effect is established by the wording of the text that establishes the cause. And it is not good to say that the cause is established by that wording of the text that establishes the effect. So it is clear from this what was mentioned regarding the definitions of 'ibarah al-nass, isharah al-nass, and iqtida' al-nass. As for the definition of dalalat al-nass, it is that which occurred with the author's statement: 'the word indicates the ruling in a thing in which there is a meaning that every language expert understands that the ruling in the spoken text is due to that meaning.' So that indication of the word is called dalalat al-nass. For example, 'Do not say to them 'uff'' indicates the prohibition of hitting by dalalat al-nass, because hitting parents is a thing in which there is the meaning of adha (harm), and adha is a meaning and cause that every one familiar with language understands that the ruling in the spoken text, i.e., its prohibition in the spoken text, is because of that meaning of adha. So the indication of the prohibition of hitting is dalalat al-nass. The reason for limiting the four types is that the intended meaning, if it is the same as that for which the word is coined, or part of that for which it is coined, or a necessary consequent that is not prior, then for those the word is 'ibarah al-nass, provided the context of the speech is for that meaning. And isharah al-nass is if the speech is not for that meaning. And if the word indicates a necessary prior of the coined meaning, then it is iqtida' al-nass. And if none of these apply, i.e., the intended meaning is neither the same as the coined meaning, nor part of it, nor a later necessary consequent, nor a prior necessary consequent, but in this meaning there exists a cause that every one familiar with language understands that the ruling in the spoken text is because of that cause, then the indication of the word for that intended meaning is dalalat al-nass. And if that type of cause does not exist, then there is no indication of any type, nor can there be inference (istidlal). And we only said that 'every one who knows the language understands' because if no one understands that meaning and cause, or some understand and some do not, then there is no indication, since verbal indication is considered relative to every person who is knowledgeable of the language. And with this condition, qiyas is excluded from the types of indication, because the meaning that serves as a cause in qiyas is not understood by every language expert, rather only a mujtahid understands it. This is an ultimate step of verification and refinement that the author presented in this place, and uncovering the aspects of indication to this extent is the author's contribution, no one preceded him in this. If you do not trust, then study the books of early and later scholars and test it. By Allah, what a contribution the author made, may Allah have mercy on him. Allah is the granter of success. As His saying: 'For the poor emigrants' (59:8). The context of this verse is that the emigrants deserve a share of the booty, and this share is obligatory and established for them, so for the entitlement and obligation this is 'ibarah al-nass. And it contains an indication that their ownership of whatever they left behind in the lands of war is nullified, because they are called 'poor' meaning they own nothing. But the verse is not directed at this, although it is part of the coined meaning, so it is isharah al-nass. And His saying: 'And upon the one to whom the child is born, their provision and clothing' (2:233). The context of this verse is that the foster mother's maintenance is obligatory upon the father of the child, so for this it is 'ibarah al-nass. And the other issues derived from this verse, since the context of the verse is not for them, so for establishing all these issues it is isharah al-nass, such as the issue that lineage is attributed to fathers, and the issue that the father has guardianship and authority to own the property of his young child by necessity, because 'al-mawludu lahu' (the one for whom the child is born) adds the child to the father with the lam of ownership, so this necessitates that
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage defines and distinguishes four types of textual indications in Hanafi usul: 'ibarah al-nass, isharah al-nass, iqtida' al-nass, and dalalat al-nass. The author begins by clarifying a logical point: the indication from cause to effect is constant (muttarid), but from effect to cause is not, because an effect can have multiple causes. The first type, 'ibarah al-nass, is the direct meaning for which the text is explicitly stated in its context. The second, isharah al-nass, is an implied meaning that is part of the coined meaning but not the main intent of the context. The third, iqtida' al-nass, is a necessary prior requirement for the text to make sense. The fourth, dalalat al-nass, is unique to the Hanafi school: it derives a ruling from a cause (illa) that is clearly understood by any native Arabic speaker as the reason for the ruling in the spoken text, even though that cause is not the direct subject of the text. For example, the verse 'Do not say to them 'uff'' prohibits even a slight expression of disrespect, but by dalalat al-nass, it also prohibits hitting parents, because hitting involves greater harm (adha), and everyone understands that the prohibition is due to that harm. The author emphasizes that the cause in dalalat al-nass is self-evident to any language expert, unlike qiyas (analogy), where only a mujtahid can identify the cause. Therefore, dalalat al-nass is a stronger proof than qiyas. The passage ends with Quranic examples: the verse about poor emigrants is 'ibarah for their entitlement to booty and isharah for the loss of their abandoned property; the verse about foster mothers is 'ibarah for the father's obligation and isharah for issues like lineage and guardianship.

Key Terms
عبارة النص ('ibarah al-nass): The explicit wording of the text that directly states the ruling for the meaning intended by the context.
اشارة النص (isharah al-nass): An implied meaning that is part of the coined meaning of the words but not the main subject of the context.
اقتضاء النص (iqtida' al-nass): A necessary prior condition for the text to be valid or meaningful.
دلالة النص (dalalat al-nass): The indication of the text to a ruling based on a cause that every language expert understands as the reason for the ruling in the spoken text.
مطرد (muttarid): Constant or concomitant; an indication that holds in all cases (e.g., cause to effect).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes dalalat al-nass from qiyas?
A) Dalalat al-nass uses a cause understood only by mujtahids.
B) Dalalat al-nass is based on a cause that every language expert understands.
C) Qiyas is stronger than dalalat al-nass.
D) Dalalat al-nass is only used in non-Quranic texts.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, dalalat al-nass is a direct textual indication stronger than qiyas because its cause is self-evident to any Arabic speaker, not requiring ijtihad.

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy
intermediate
8 min
Dalaalat al-Nass and Muqtada al-Kalam
Hierarchy of textual indications and muqtada example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi hierarchy of textual indications (ibara, ishara, dalaalat al-nass, qiyas) and apply muqtada al-kalam to derive implied rulings from speech.

Core Idea
Dalaalat al-nass is definitive but yields to ibara/ishara; it ranks above qiyas but cannot establish hudud.

This passage lays out the binding force of dalaalat al-nass (implication of the text) within the Hanafi usul framework. You will see how it compares to explicit wording and gesture, why it is stronger than analogy, and when it fails—specifically for hudud and qisas. The concept of muqtada al-kalam (requisite of speech) then brings theory to life with a concrete example of a manumission command that implies a prior sale.

Guided Path
1
Map the hierarchy of textual indications
List the four key indications mentioned: ibarat al-nass (explicit wording), isharat al-nass (gesture/pointer), dalaalat al-nass (implication), and qiyas (analogy). Note their relative strengths according to the text.
The author places dalaalat al-nass above qiyas and even above khabar wahid, but below ibara and ishara in cases of conflict.
2
Understand the conflict resolution rule
When ibara/ishara conflict with dalaalat, the former take precedence because they are established by both the wording and its linguistic meaning. If ibara and ishara themselves conflict, ibara wins due to context (sawq al-kalam).
This ordering is crucial for preferring stronger over weaker textual indications.
3
Identify the limitation of dalaalat al-nass
The text states that dalaalat al-nass cannot establish hudud and qisas because of the hadith 'Repel the hudud by doubts.' This is a key boundary: implications derived from meaning are not sufficient to remove doubts in criminal punishments.
This shows that even a strong source can have exceptions based on overriding principles.
4
Analyze the muqtada al-kalam example
Consider the command 'Free your slave from me for a thousand.' The utterance logically requires (muqtada) that the person commanded first owns the slave. Ownership transfer at this point can only occur through a sale, and the phrase 'for a thousand' indicates a price. Thus, the statement implies a sale for the manumission to be valid.
Muqtada al-kalam fills in what must be true for a statement to make sense, deriving legal consequences from necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثابت بدلالة النص كالثابت بالعبارة والاشارة يعني جو مسئلہ دلالتہ النص کے ساتھ ثابت ہو گا وہ برابر اور مساوی ہوگا فی الثبوت والقطعیہ اس مسئلہ کے ساتھ جو عبارۃ النص یا اشارہ النص کے ساتھ ثابت ہے الا عند التعارض مگر بوقت تعارض کے عبارۃ النص اور اشارۃ النص کو ترجیح حاصل ہو گی علی دلالۃ النص کیونکہ عبارة اور اشارة ثابت بالنظم وبالمعنى اللغوى ہیں اور دلالۃ النص ثابت بالمعنی ہے فقط اور اگر عبارۃ النص اور اشارۃ النص میں تعارض ہو جاتے تو پھر عبارۃ النص کو ترجیح ہوگی کیونکہ سوق کلام عبارة النص کے لئے موجب ترجیح ہے۔ وھو فوق القیاس اور دلالہ النص قیاس سے فائق ہے بلکہ خبر واحد پر بھی اسے فوقیت حاصل ہے لان المعنی فی القیاس کیونکہ معنی یعنی وہ علتہ جس کی وجہ سے قیاس کیا جاتا ہے اس کا ادراک من النص بالر ہی ہوتا ہے اور دلالہ النص اس کا ادراک لغتہ ہوتا ہے۔ فیثبت بہا ماین درتی بالشبہات جو اشیا مندری بالشھات ہوتی ہیں یعنی حدود و قصاص جن کے متعلق رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے اور ڈا الحدود بالشحات یہ اشیاء دلالۃ النص کے ساتھ ثابت نہیں ہو سکتی ۔ واعلم ان في بعض المسائل اور مسائل مذکورہ فی المتن میں اس بارے میں کلام ہے کہ یہ ثابت بدلالة النص ہیں یا ثابت بالقياس فعلیک بالتا عمل آپ غور و فکر کریں بہر حال وہ مصنف کے نزدیک دلالۃ النص کے ساتھ ثابت ہیں۔ داھا المقتضی کلام مقتضی کی مثال دى بقوله نحو اعتق عبدك عنى بالف يقتضى البيع یہ کلام تقاضا کرتی ہے بیع کا تو اعتق عبدک عنی بالف یہ مقتضی ہے اور بیع اس کا مقتضا ہے۔ ضرورة صحة العشق کیونکہ آمر کی جانب سے صحتہ عتق اس کے بغیر ہو نہیں سکتی کیونکہ ایک شخص اپنے غلام کو دوسرے شخص کی جانب سے وکاله و نیابتہ آزاد نہیں کر سکتا جب تک اس دوسرے شخص کے ملک میں نہ دیدے اور سینب ملک اس مقام پر بیع ہی ہو سکتی ہے اور بالف یہ قرینہ بیع ہے کہ مبادلہ
And what is established by implication of the text (dalaalat al-nass) is like what is established by explicit wording (ibara) and gesture (ishara), meaning that the ruling established by implication of the text will be equal in strength and definitiveness to that established by ibara or ishara, except in case of conflict; then at the time of conflict, ibara and ishara are given preference over dalaalat al-nass, because ibara and ishara are established by the wording and its linguistic meaning, while dalaalat al-nass is established by meaning alone. And if ibara and ishara conflict, then ibara is given preference, because the context of speech (sawq al-kalam) gives preference to ibara. And it (dalaalat al-nass) is above qiyas (analogy). And dalaalat al-nass is superior to qiyas, indeed it is even superior to khabar wahid (solitary report), because the meaning (i.e., the effective cause) in qiyas is perceived from the text by opinion (ra'y), while in dalaalat al-nass it is perceived from language. So it does not establish matters that are repelled by shubuhat (doubts), i.e., hudud and qisas, regarding which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Repel the hudud by shubuhat.' These matters cannot be established by dalaalat al-nass. And know that in some issues mentioned in the matn there is discussion about whether they are established by dalaalat al-nass or by qiyas, so you should reflect. However, those issues are established by dalaalat al-nass according to the author. Then the example of muqtada al-kalam (requisite of speech): the saying 'Free your slave from me for a thousand' requires a sale. This statement demands a sale, so 'Free your slave from me for a thousand' is the muqtadi (requirer) and the sale is its muqtada (required thing) due to the necessity of the validity of the manumission, because a person cannot free his own slave on behalf of another by agency until he first gives him into the other's ownership, and ownership at this point can only be through a sale, and the phrase 'for a thousand' is a qarinah (indicator) of exchange.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage is an usul rule explaining the status of dalaalat al-nass (implication of the text) within the Hanafi hierarchy of textual indications. The author states that dalaalat al-nass has the same definitive force as ibara (explicit expression) and ishara (gesture/pointer) in establishing rulings, except when they conflict; then ibara and ishara are preferred because they are based on both the wording and linguistic meaning, while dalaalat al-nass is based only on meaning. The superiority order is: ibara > ishara > dalaalat al-nass > qiyas (analogy) and khabar wahid. A key point is that dalaalat al-nass cannot establish punishments such as hudud and qisas because these are repelled by shubuhat (doubts) as per the hadith. The author notes that some issues in the matn are debated whether they fall under dalaalat al-nass or qiyas, but the author holds they are dalaalat al-nass. Finally, an example of muqtada al-kalam (the requisite of speech) is given: someone says 'Free your slave from me for a thousand' – this statement necessitates a sale because freeing on behalf of another requires ownership, which can only be achieved through a sale here. The phrase 'for a thousand' indicates an exchange. This is a key illustration of how a statement can imply a legal transaction not explicitly mentioned.

Key Terms
دلالۃ النص (dalaalat al-nass): Implication of the text: a ruling derived from the meaning of the text beyond its literal words, using linguistic context.
مقتضیٰ الکلام (muqtada al-kalam): The requisite of speech: what is necessarily implied by a statement for it to be valid and meaningful.
عبارۃ النص (ibarat al-nass): Explicit wording of the text, the primary indication.
اشارۃ النص (isharat al-nass): Gesture or pointer of the text: a secondary indication that points to a ruling through implication or context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following cannot be established by dalaalat al-nass?
A) The obligation of zakat on certain properties
B) The prohibition of riba
C) The punishment of hadd for theft (sariqa)
D) The validity of marriage contracts

Key Takeaway
Dalaalat al-nass holds a definitive but secondary position in the Hanafi textual hierarchy, ranking above qiyas but below ibara and ishara, and cannot be used to establish hudud.

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy

Distinguishing Mahdhūf from Muqtada in Dalāla
Clarifying that mahdhūf (deleted) is included in the four types of dalāla.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mahdhūf and muqtada in Hanafi usul and explain why mahdhūf does not constitute a fifth type of dalāla.

Core Idea
A deleted word (mahdhūf) is like an uttered word in ruling, so its meaning indication fits the four types—no fifth type needed.

In learning about the four types of dalāla (ibāra, ishāra, dalāla, iqtida'), some scholars mistakenly considered mahdhūf (deleted word) as a subset of muqtada (implicit meaning). This led to an objection: if mahdhūf is not part of muqtada, wouldn't there be a fifth type? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi response, showing that mahdhūf is covered by the existing four types because it is treated in the ruling of an uttered word.

Guided Path
1
Identify the confusion
Some scholars treated mahdhūf as part of muqtada. Understand why this is wrong: mahdhūf is an omitted word, while muqtada is a required implicit meaning.
2
State the objection
If mahdhūf is not in muqtada, then there would be a fifth type of dalāla beyond the four, breaking the division.
3
Explain the Hanafi response
The four types apply to 'words indicating meanings.' Mahdhūf, though not uttered, is linguistically established and thus considered in the ruling of an uttered word. Therefore, the uttered word indicates the mahdhūf, and the mahdhūf indicates its meaning via one of the four types.
4
Differentiate between two types of indication
Dalāla al-lafz 'alā al-lafz (indication of a word for a word) is not a meaning-indication; it is a prerequisite. Only dalāla al-lafz 'alā al-ma'na is divided into four.
5
Conclude
Mahdhūf is not a fifth type; it is included because its meaning indication falls under the four types.

وقوله وهما يتصل بذلك اى بالمقتضى هو المحذوف یعنی محذوف ملحق اور متصل مقتضی کے ساتھ واعلم انه يشتبه بعض الناس پر محذوف مشتبہ بالمقتضیٰ ہو گیا ہے حتی کہ اتحفہ نے محذوف کو مقتضیٰ میں درج کر دیا ہے۔ انھوں ولا يعرفون الفرق بينهما جو محذوف اور مقتضیٰ کے مابین فرق تھا وہ انھیں معلوم نہیں ہوا اس بنا پر انھوں نے ایک کو دوسرے کا حکم دیا اور بہت سے احکام کے اندر غلطی میں مبتلا ہوئے وان توهم متوهم اگر کسی کو وہم ہو کہ جب محذوف مقتضی میں درج نہیں ہے تو پھر عبارہ اور اشارہ اور دلالہ اور اقتضا کے علاوہ یہ قسم خامس برائے استدلال ہوگا تو حصر فی الا ربعہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔ فهذا وهم باطل تو یہ وہم باطل ہے لان مرادنا باللفظ الدال على المعنی کیونکہ جو ہم نے لفظ دال علی المعنیٰ کو ان اقسام اربعہ کے لئے مورد قسمہ بنایا ہے ہماری مراد اس لفظ سے عام ہے خواہ وہ حقیقتاً لفظ ہو یا حكماً فكل ما هو محذوف پس سر وہ لفظ جو محذوف ہے اگر چہ وہ ملفوظ حقیقی نہیں لیکن لغتہ وہ ثابت ہے فانه في حكم الملفوظ تو وہ حکم ملفوظ میں ہے نیكون اللفظ المنطوق تو لفظ منطوق لفظ محذوف پر دال ہے اور یہ لفظ محذوف اپنے معنی پر ان اقسام اربعہ کے موافق دال ہوگا۔ فالدلالة المنقسمة دلالہ جس کی تقسیم اقسام اربعہ کی طرف کی گئی ہے وہ دلالتہ اللفظ على المعنی ہے اور مجذوف میں بھی دلالۃ اللفظ على المعنی موجود ہے لہذا یہ بھی اسی تقسیم میں درج ہوگا. اما دلالت اللفظ علی لفظ باقی رہی دلالہ اللفظ على اللفظ یہ از قبیلہ دلالة اللفظ على المعنی نہیں ہے لہذا جو دلالۃ المنطوق على المحذوف ہے وہ ان اقسام کی طرف منقسم نہیں ہوگی ۔
His statement: 'And it is connected to that, i.e., to the muqtada, is the mahdhūf.' That is, the deleted (mahdhūf) is annexed and connected to the muqtada. And know that some people became confused—the mahdhūf became confused with the muqtada, such that someone (maybe 'Ata' or 'Utfa') included the mahdhūf under the muqtada. They did not know the difference between them. Therefore, they treated one as the other and fell into error in many rulings. And if someone imagines that when mahdhūf is not included in muqtada, then besides ibāra, ishāra, dalāla, and iqtida', this would be a fifth type of inference, making the division into four invalid. So this is a false imagination. Because our meaning by 'the word indicating the meaning' — since we made the word indicating the meaning the subject of division into these four types, our meaning by 'word' is general, whether it is a word in reality or by ruling. So everything that is mahdhūf — the word that is deleted, even though it is not an actual uttered word, but linguistically it is established, so it is in the ruling of an uttered word. Thus the uttered word (mantuq) indicates the deleted word, and this deleted word will indicate its meaning in accordance with these four types. Therefore, the dalāla that is divided into four types is the indication of a word for a meaning, and in the mahdhūf, there is also indication of a word for a meaning, so it is included in this division. As for the indication of a word for a word, that remains—it is not of the category of indication of a word for a meaning, so the indication of the uttered for the deleted is not divisible into these types.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This is a critical refinement passage where the commentator clarifies a common confusion between mahdhūf (deleted/omitted word) and muqtada (implicit meaning required by necessity). Some scholars, including one named 'Ata' or 'Utfa', mistakenly treated mahdhūf as a subset of muqtada. The author refutes this by explaining the difference: muqtada is an implicit meaning that is necessary for the utterance, while mahdhūf is a word that has been omitted from the utterance but is understood from context. This leads to an objection: if mahdhūf is not part of muqtada, then there would be a fifth type of dalāla beyond the well-known four (ibāra, ishāra, dalāla, iqtida'). The author responds that mahdhūf is not a separate division because the four types apply to 'words indicating meanings', and mahdhūf, though not uttered, is considered a word in ruling (hukm al-malfūz) because it is linguistically understood. The uttered word indicates the mahdhūf, and then the mahdhūf indicates its meaning through one of the four types. So the four types are sufficient. The indication of a word for a word (e.g., the uttered for the omitted) is not itself a dalāla type; it is a prerequisite. This is a precise point in usul al-fiqh about the scope of the four-fold division of dalāla.

Key Terms
محذوف (mahdhūf): A word that is omitted from an utterance but understood from context, considered in the ruling of an uttered word for dalāla purposes.
مقتضیٰ (muqtada): An implicit meaning that is necessarily required for the utterance to be valid, established by iqtida'.
دلالة اللفظ على اللفظ (dalāla al-lafz 'alā al-lafz): Indication of a word for another word (e.g., the uttered word for the omitted word). This is not considered a type of dalāla in the four-fold division because it is not indication of a word for a meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul scholars in this passage, why is mahdhūf (deleted word) not considered a fifth type of dalāla beyond the four?
A) Because mahdhūf is actually a subset of iqtida'.
B) Because mahdhūf is considered in the ruling of an uttered word, so its indication of meaning falls under the four types.
C) Because mahdhūf indicates words, not meanings.
D) Because mahdhūf is not recognized in Hanafi usul.

Key Takeaway
Mahdhūf is not a fifth type of dalāla because it is treated as an uttered word in ruling, so its meaning indication falls under the existing four types.
