Rejecting Baseless Probabilities in Linguistic Interpretation
Rational argument that accepting baseless probabilities destroys all realities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why baseless probabilities (ihtimalat bila dalil) are rejected in Hanafi usul and apply this principle to preserve the stability of linguistic realities (haqa'iq).

Core Idea
Baseless probabilities invalidate all realities, resembling sophistry; thus they are ignored in textual interpretation.

In Hanafi usul, the apparent meaning (zahir) of a text is authoritative unless there is evidence (dalil) to the contrary. This lesson examines a key rational argument: if every remote possibility were considered, then even the reality of a person sitting before us could be doubted. The author explains that such baseless probabilities would destroy both the realities of things and the realities of words. Therefore, only probabilities supported by evidence are valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem: What is a baseless probability?
A baseless probability is a possibility that has no evidence (qarinah) to support it. For example, the possibility that Zayd sitting before you is not actually Zayd because he could have died and been replaced.
This is a purely theoretical possibility with no supporting evidence.
2
Follow the reductio ad absurdum
If such baseless probabilities are accepted as valid, then no reality can be established. Even the identity of a person or the meaning of a word could be doubted constantly.
This leads to an infinite regress of doubt.
3
Recognize the consequence: Sophism
The position that denies all objective reality is exactly the doctrine of the Sophists (sufastaiyyah). Islam rejects this, affirming that reality is stable and knowable.
The Hanafi school aligns with the mainstream Islamic rejection of absolute skepticism.
4
Apply to linguistic texts
Similarly, every word has theoretical possibilities of abrogation, specification, homonymy, or metaphor. But without evidence, these do not affect the apparent meaning (zahir). The text remains authoritative unless a valid probability is supported by a dalil.
This preserves the reliability of scripture and legal language.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
توقف ہے جہاں احتمال پیدا ہو جائے وہاں توقف کرنا لازم ہے اس کو باطل کر رہا ہے ۔ کہ اگر اس قسم کا احتمال معتبر سمجھا جائے تو یہ ایک ایسا احتمال ہے جو سطل الحقائق حقائق اشیا کو باطل کر دے گا یمکن ان یراد به یعنی یبطل الحقائق میں لفظ حقائق سے مراد حقائق الاشیاء ہوں یعنی اگر اس قسم کے احتمالات کو معتبر قرار دیا جائے تو پھر حقائق اشیاء باطل ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ مجوز ان لا يكون زيد أ جو شخص زید ہمارے سامنے بیٹھا ہے یہ زید نہ ہو کیونکہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ زید منعدم ہو چکا ہو اور اس کی جگہ کوئی اور شخص پیدا ہو چکا ہے اگر اس قسم کا احتمال معتبر ہو تو پھر حقائق اشیاء ثابت نہیں سکتیں اور دھو عين مذهب السوفسطائية یہ بعینہ سو فسطانیہ کا مذہب ہے جو حقائق اشیاء کی نفی اور انکار کرتے ہیں ويمكن ان يراد به حقائق الالفاظ یعنی لفظ حقائق سے مراد حقائق الفاظ ہوں کیونکہ کوئی ایسا لفظ نہیں ہے جس کے اندر احتمال قریب یا بعید نسخ یا خصوص یا اشتراک یا مجازہ کا نہ ہو بلکہ سر لفظ میں اس قسم کا احتمال پیدا ہو سکتا ہے۔ جو فان اعتبرت هذه الاحتمالات اگر اس قسم کے احتمالات بلا قرینہ معتبر سمجھے جائیں تو پھر الفاظ کی دلالت اپنے معانی موضوع لہ پر باطل ہو جائے اور یہی دلالتہ علی الموضوع لہ الفاظ کی حقیقت ہے پھر یہ حقیقت ان احتمالات کی بنیاد پر باطل ہو جائیگی - وايضا لم تدع انه محکم یہ ایک اور جواب ہے حاصل یہ کہ ہم اس کے مدعی نہیں ہیں کہ امر کسی ایک معنی مثلاً وجوب میں محکم ہے جس کے خلاف احتمال بالکل نہ ہو۔ نہ ناشی بالدلیل نہ ناشی بلا دلیل بلکہ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ معنی وجوب میں ظاہبر کا درجہ رکھتا ہے جس میں احتمالات ناشی بلا دلیل پیدا ہو سکتے ہیں جو کہ معتبر نہیں ہوتے
It is that where probability occurs, stopping is necessary. This refutes that. Because if this kind of probability is considered valid, it is a probability that would invalidate the realities of things. It can be intended by that, meaning 'invalidates the realities' – by 'realities' is meant the realities of things. So if such probabilities are considered valid, then the realities of things would become invalid, because it could be that Zayd sitting before us is not Zayd, since Zayd may have perished and another person has been created in his place. If this kind of probability is valid, then realities cannot be established, and this is exactly the doctrine of the Sophists who deny and reject the realities of things. And it can be intended to mean the realities of words, because there is no word in which there is not a near or far probability of abrogation, specification, homonymy, or metaphor; rather, every word can have such probability. Then, if these probabilities without evidence are considered valid, then the indication of words to their original meanings would become invalid, and this indication is the reality of words. Then this reality would be invalidated on the basis of these probabilities. And also we do not claim that it is muhkam – this is another answer. The conclusion is that we do not claim that the command is muhkam in one meaning, e.g., obligation, absolutely without any probability, neither arising from evidence nor without evidence. Rather we say that the meaning of the word in obligation has the rank of zahir, in which probabilities not arising from evidence can occur, but they are not considered valid.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage discusses the rejection of baseless probabilities (ihtimalat bila dalil) in usul al-fiqh. The author argues that if every remote possibility were considered valid, such as the possibility that a person known as Zayd might not actually be Zayd because he could have died and been replaced, then no reality (haqiqah) could be established. This would lead to the doctrine of the Sophists, who deny objective reality. Similarly, in linguistic interpretation, every word can theoretically have multiple possibilities (abrogation, specification, etc.), but if we accept all such possibilities without evidence (qarinah), then the stable meaning of words would be lost. The Hanafi position is that the command (amr) is not muhkam (absolutely unambiguous) but is zahir (apparent), meaning it can have probabilities not arising from evidence, but those probabilities are not considered valid in deriving rulings. This principle preserves the reliability of linguistic evidence in jurisprudence.

Key Terms
احتمال (ihtimal): A possibility or probability that may affect the interpretation of a text.
حقائق (haqā'iq): Realities; here refers to either the realities of things (haqā'iq al-ashyā') or the realities of words (haqā'iq al-alfāz).
محکم (muhkam): A text that is absolutely clear and unambiguous with no room for probability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are baseless probabilities (ihtimalat bila dalil) not considered valid in Hanafi usul?
A) Because they lead to doubt in all realities, resembling the Sophist doctrine.
B) Because they are only valid in the case of amr (command).
C) Because they are supported by qiyas (analogy).
D) Because the scholars agreed to ignore them unanimously.

Key Takeaway
Baseless probabilities (ihtimalat bila dalil) are rejected in Hanafi usul because accepting them would undermine the stability of both objective realities and linguistic meanings.

Three Types of Payment (Ada) in Huquq al-‘Ibad
Defines and gives examples of the three types of payment in huquq al-‘ibad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ada kamil, ada qasir, and shabih al-qada, and identify examples of each from the Hanafi usul text.

Core Idea
Payment in rights of humans is classified by item condition and ownership: complete, deficient, or resembling qada.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the fulfillment of obligations (ada) in huquq al-‘ibad is not monolithic. Scholars distinguish three types based on the state of the delivered item: whether it is the exact same as owed (kamil), defective (qasir), or involves a change of ownership but is still considered payment (shabih al-qada). This classification determines legal consequences such as discharge of liability and the right to compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types
Read the passage and note the three categories: ada kamil, ada qasir, shabih al-qada. Understand each definition as presented.
2
Analyze the conditions for ada kamil
Complete ada requires delivering the very same specific item (ayn) in its original condition. Study the examples: return of usurped property, delivery of sold goods unchanged, and delivery in sarf/salam contracts despite the obligation being a debt.
The sarf/salam example is tricky: the lawgiver treats the delivered item as the very right to avoid prohibited substitution before possession.
3
Examine ada qasir
Deficient ada occurs when the item is delivered with a new defect or encumbrance (e.g., a slave who commits a crime, becomes pregnant, or gets sick during usurpation). Note that the defect arises after the contract but before delivery.
4
Understand shabih al-qada
This type involves a change in the ownership chain: the item delivered was originally owned by the creditor, then transferred, and later reacquired by the debtor. The example is a woman's father set as mahr, claimed by a third party, then reacquired by the husband. Despite ownership change, the delivery is considered ada.
5
Connect to legal effect
Recognize that the classification directly affects whether the debtor is discharged and the creditor's rights to return the item or claim damages. This is especially clear in the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the effect of defects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

پر تفریح ہے اگر یہ مبیع مشغول بالجنایت اسی جنایت میں قتل ہو کر ہلاک ہوا تو انتقض القبض عند ابي حنيفه تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ قبض باطل ہو جائیگی کان المشترى لم يقبض لهذا مشتری کل شمن کار جوع کرے گا عن البائع وعندهما هذا عیب اور صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ ایک عیب ہے اور عیب تمامیہ تسلیم اور قبض سے مانع نہیں ہوتا لہذا مشتری کی قبض تام ہو چکی ہے کا داء الزيوف جیسے کوئی شخص اپنے قرضہ میں قرض خواہ کو دراہم زیوف ادا کرتا ہے اور صاحب الحق کو علم نہیں ہوتا تو یہ قبض تام ہو جاتی ہے حتى لو هلك عنده اگر یہ عبد مشغول مشتری کے ہاں بلاک ہوا تو اس کا حق باطل ہو جائیگا رجوع بالثمن کلہا تو نہیں کر سکتا البتہ رجوع بالنقصان ہوگا اور اسی طرح اختلاف ہو گا جارہ یہ منصوبہ میں جو غاصب کے ہاں حاملہ ہوئی ہے پھر اس نے واپس کی ہے اور مالک کے ہاں اسی سبب سے ہلاک ہوئی ہے تو امام کے نزدیک تمام قیمت کی ضمان مناصب پر لازم ہوگی ۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک ضمان نہیں ہوگی۔ والاداء الذي يشبه القضاء كما اذا المهراباها نا ستحق صورۃ مسئلہ یوں ہے ایک عورت کا باپ کسی شخص کا عبدو غلام تھا اس شخص نے اس عورت کے ساتھ نکاح کیا اور اس عورت کا باپ حق المہر میں معین کر دیا تو عورت نفس عقد کے ساتھ اپنے والد کی مالک ہو چکی ہے اور وہ ازاد ہو جائیں گے ۔ من ملک زارحم محرم فصو ر کی وجہ سے فاستحق اور یہ عبد یعنی ابوالمرا مستحق ہو ا یعنی کسی اور شخص نے دعوی کر دیا کہ یہ میرا غلام ہے اور قاضی نے اس کے حق میں فیصلہ دیدیا تو عورت کا ملک اور عتق باطل ہو جائیں گے اور زوج پر اس کی قیمت واجب ہو جائیگی وان لم يقض القاضی یعنی قاضی نے فیصلہ نہیں دیا نہ استحقاق کا اور نہ وجوب قیمہ على الزوج کا حتی ملکه ثانیا حتی کہ زوج اس عبید کا جو ابو المرآۃ ہے ثانیا مالک ہو گیا ہے بشرا ہوا دھبہ تو زوج پر لازم ہے کہ یہ عبد عورت کے حوالہ کرے تو یہ تسلیم ادا ہے بایں حیثیت کہ مہبی عبد عین سے حق المرآة کا جس کی وہ مستحق محقى بالقسمينة في عقد النكاح پس یہ تسلیم من حيث انه عين حقها اداء چونکہ یہی غلام عین ہے حق عورت کا تو اسی حیثیت سے تسلیم عبد ا دا ہوگی فلا يملك منعہ تو جب عورت مطالبہ کرے یہی معبد جو میرا باپ ہے میرے حوالہ کر تو خاوند اس کو اس عورت سے نہیں روک سکتا یہ سب کچھ بحیثت ادا ہونے کے ہے۔ دمن حیث انه ان تبدل الملك الخ اور بائیں حیثیت کہ اس غلام پر تبدل ملک ہو چکا ہے کیونکہ صاحب الحق کے ملک سے خارج ہو کر زوج کے ملک میں آیا ہے اور تبدل ملک
Reciting in the state of ruku is like reciting in qiyam, so it is similar to ada. And rights of humans (huquq al-ibad) are also divided into these types: within them occur the three types of complete ada, deficient ada, and that resembling qada. As for complete ada: in huquq al-ibad, we present several examples of complete ada: returning the very same right in usurpation, like the usurper returns the very same thing he usurped, and it is also in the same state and description as at the time of usurpation. And the sale: i.e., delivering the very same right in sale, meaning the seller delivers the sold item in the same state as at the time of the sale contract. And sarf and salam: i.e., delivering the very same right in the contract of sarf and salam: in a sarf sale, the delivery of the counter-value of sarf, and in a salam sale, the delivery of the muslam fihi is the delivery of the very same right. When a person makes a sarf contract or a salam contract, then the counter-value in sarf and the muslam fihi in salam become owed as a debt (dayn), similar to a debt where its replacement is owed as a debt. And this being owed as a debt is an attribute that does not admit of delivery and handing over. Therefore, giving the counter-value and muslam fihi in exchange for this attribute should have been qada, because these specific items (ayn) are other than the debt, i.e., what was owed as a debt was a dayn, and this specific item is other than it, so it should have been qada. However, the Lawgiver declared this delivered specific item as the very right (ayn) for that owed debt, so that substitution (istibdal) in sarf and salam before qabd would not become necessary, which is prohibited by sharia. If this delivered item were not declared as the very right, but the original obligation was merely the attribute of being owed as a debt, and this delivered item were considered its replacement, then substitution before qabd would become necessary, which is prohibited. Therefore, the delivered item is the very right; its payment is complete ada. And the deficient (qasir): like returning the usurped item or sold item while it is occupied with something else. An example of deficient ada in huquq al-ibad: a usurper usurped a slave who was free from defects, but when he returned it, it was occupied with a crime, e.g., the slave killed someone or cut off someone's hand, or occupied with a debt, e.g., he destroyed someone's property for which he is liable, or he became sick, and all these things occurred while he was in the usurper's possession. Similarly, a female slave who was non-pregnant when usurped, but when returned she is pregnant, and this pregnancy occurred in the usurper's possession; this is deficient ada. Similarly, a seller sold a male or female slave; at the time of sale, the sold item was free from defects; when the buyer later took possession, the sold item was defective with one of the mentioned defects; this is also deficient ada. Even if he [the buyer] gets possession by that cause, this is a branch on its being deficient. If this sold item, occupied with a crime, died as a result of that crime, then the possession is invalidated according to Abu Hanifa. So according to Abu Hanifa, this possession becomes void, as if the buyer had not taken possession. Therefore, the buyer will return the full price to the seller. According to them (the Sahibayn), this is a defect, and a defect does not prevent complete delivery and possession. Therefore, the buyer's possession is complete, like the payment of counterfeit (ziyuf) dirhams. For example, a person pays counterfeit dirhams to the creditor for his debt, and the creditor is unaware; this possession is complete. Even if this occupied slave perishes at the buyer's, his right is void; he cannot return the full price, but he can return the deficiency. And similarly, the dispute will be concerning the female slave who became pregnant at the usurper's, then he returned her, and she perished at the owner's due to the same cause: according to the Imam, the usurper is liable for the full value; according to the Sahibayn, there is no liability. And the payment that resembles qada: like when the father of a woman is a slave of a person, then that person marries the woman and appoints her father as the dowry (mahr). Then the woman becomes the owner of her father by the contract itself, and he becomes free due to the rule: 'Whoever owns a mahram relative, he becomes free.' Then this slave (the woman's father) becomes claimed (mustahaqq), i.e., another person claims that he is his slave, and the judge decides in his favor. Then the woman's ownership and emancipation become void, and the husband becomes liable for his value. And if the judge does not decide (neither for the claim nor for the liability of the value on the husband), until he (the husband) becomes the owner of this slave (the woman's father) a second time, then the husband is obliged to hand over this slave to the woman. This delivery is ada in the sense that the slave is the very right of the woman (ayn haqq al-mar'ah) that she is entitled to as the mahr in the marriage contract. So this delivery, in that it is her very right, is ada. Therefore, he cannot prevent her. When the woman demands, 'Hand over this slave who is my father to me,' the husband cannot withhold him from her. This is all from the perspective of its being ada. And from the perspective that the ownership of this slave has changed because it left the owner's possession and came into the husband's possession, and the change of ownership...
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary explains the classification of payment (ada') in the rights of humans (huquq al-ibad). The author first notes that rights of humans are divided into three types of payment: complete (kamil), deficient (qasir), and that resembling qada (shabih al-qada). He then provides examples. Complete ada involves delivering the very same specific item (ayn) that is owed in its original condition. Examples include returning the very item usurped, delivering the sold item as it was at contract, and in currency exchange (sarf) and salam contracts, where the specific counter-value or muslam fihi is treated as the very right owed to avoid prohibited substitution before possession. Deficient ada occurs when the item is delivered with a new defect or encumbrance, such as a slave who commits a crime or becomes pregnant while in the usurper's possession. This leads to a dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that such defects invalidate the possession (qabd) entirely, so the buyer can return the item and get a full refund. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) view the defect as a mere flaw that does not prevent possession; the buyer can only claim a reduction in price. The third type, resembling qada, is illustrated by a case where a woman's father is a slave, the husband marries her and sets the father as mahr, the father becomes free by relative ownership, then a third party successfully claims him, and later the husband reacquires him. In this scenario, the husband must deliver the slave to the wife, which is considered ada because the slave is the very right she is owed as mahr, despite the change in ownership. The text is cut off at the end of this example.

Key Terms
اداء (ada): Fulfillment of an obligation by delivering the right
اداء کامل (ada kamil): Delivering the very specific item owed in its original state
اداء قاصر (ada qasir): Delivery of an item with a new defect or encumbrance
شبيه بالقضاء (shabih al-qada): Payment that is legally ada but involves a change in ownership of the thing delivered
قبض (qabd): Taking possession of an item

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of ada kamil according to the passage?
A) Returning a usurped slave who committed a crime while in the usurper's possession
B) Delivering the exact counter-value in a sarf contract
C) Returning a female slave who became pregnant during usurpation
D) Paying a debt with counterfeit dirhams

Key Takeaway
The classification of payment into complete, deficient, and resembling qada depends on the condition and ownership of the delivered item, not just the act of delivery.

The Effect of Defects on Possession: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Presents the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether defects invalidate possession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the effect of defects on possession (qabd) and identify the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
A defect arising before delivery split Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn: possession is either voided or merely flawed.

In the previous lesson, we learned that deficient ada (ada qasir) occurs when an item is delivered with a new defect. But what is the legal effect of such a delivery? This is where a significant intra-Hanafi disagreement arises. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that a defect which makes the item no longer as contracted invalidates the possession entirely (intiqad al-qabd), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it a mere defect that does not prevent valid possession, only entitling the buyer to a reduction in price. This disagreement has concrete consequences for the rights of the parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
Focus on the scenario in the passage where a sold slave becomes defective (e.g., commits a crime) before delivery. The key question: does the defect invalidate the buyer's possession (qabd)?
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and dalil
Abu Hanifa holds that possession is invalidated (intaqada al-qabd). His reasoning: the delivery is deficient because the item is not as owed; therefore, it is as if possession never occurred. The buyer can return the item and demand the full price.
The passage says: 'then the possession is invalidated according to Abu Hanifa'
3
State the Sahibayn's position and dalil
The Sahibayn hold that the defect does not invalidate possession; it is merely a defect allowing a reduction in price. Their reasoning: the defect does not prevent delivery; possession is complete, analogous to paying with counterfeit dirhams.
The passage compares this to paying debt with counterfeit coins – possession is complete.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference emerges if the defective item perishes after delivery. Under Abu Hanifa, since possession is void, the risk remains with the seller and the buyer can recover the full price. Under the Sahibayn, the buyer bears the risk and can only claim the deficiency.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The passage does not indicate a preferred view; it presents both positions neutrally. Later Hanafi works may give tarjih. In some contexts, the Sahibayn's view is considered more practical, but both are transmitted.

استحقاق کا اور نہ وجوب قیمہ على الزوج کا حتی ملکه ثانیا حتی کہ زوج اس عبید کا جو ابو المرآۃ ہے ثانیا مالک ہو گیا ہے بشرا ہوا دھبہ تو زوج پر لازم ہے کہ یہ عبد عورت کے حوالہ کرے تو یہ تسلیم ادا ہے بایں حیثیت کہ مہبی عبد عین سے حق المرآة کا جس کی وہ مستحق محقى بالقسمينة في عقد النكاح پس یہ تسلیم من حيث انه عين حقها اداء چونکہ یہی غلام عین ہے حق عورت کا تو اسی حیثیت سے تسلیم عبد ا دا ہوگی فلا يملك منعہ تو جب عورت مطالبہ کرے یہی معبد جو میرا باپ ہے میرے حوالہ کر تو خاوند اس کو اس عورت سے نہیں روک سکتا یہ سب کچھ بحیثت ادا ہونے کے ہے۔ دمن حیث انه ان تبدل الملك الخ اور بائیں حیثیت کہ اس غلام پر تبدل ملک ہو چکا ہے کیونکہ صاحب الحق کے ملک سے خارج ہو کر زوج کے ملک میں آیا ہے اور تبدل ملک
Reciting in the state of ruku is like reciting in qiyam, so it is similar to ada. And rights of humans (huquq al-ibad) are also divided into these types: within them occur the three types of complete ada, deficient ada, and that resembling qada. As for complete ada: in huquq al-ibad, we present several examples of complete ada: returning the very same right in usurpation, like the usurper returns the very same thing he usurped, and it is also in the same state and description as at the time of usurpation. And the sale: i.e., delivering the very same right in sale, meaning the seller delivers the sold item in the same state as at the time of the sale contract. And sarf and salam: i.e., delivering the very same right in the contract of sarf and salam: in a sarf sale, the delivery of the counter-value of sarf, and in a salam sale, the delivery of the muslam fihi is the delivery of the very same right. When a person makes a sarf contract or a salam contract, then the counter-value in sarf and the muslam fihi in salam become owed as a debt (dayn), similar to a debt where its replacement is owed as a debt. And this being owed as a debt is an attribute that does not admit of delivery and handing over. Therefore, giving the counter-value and muslam fihi in exchange for this attribute should have been qada, because these specific items (ayn) are other than the debt, i.e., what was owed as a debt was a dayn, and this specific item is other than it, so it should have been qada. However, the Lawgiver declared this delivered specific item as the very right (ayn) for that owed debt, so that substitution (istibdal) in sarf and salam before qabd would not become necessary, which is prohibited by sharia. If this delivered item were not declared as the very right, but the original obligation was merely the attribute of being owed as a debt, and this delivered item were considered its replacement, then substitution before qabd would become necessary, which is prohibited. Therefore, the delivered item is the very right; its payment is complete ada. And the deficient (qasir): like returning the usurped item or sold item while it is occupied with something else. An example of deficient ada in huquq al-ibad: a usurper usurped a slave who was free from defects, but when he returned it, it was occupied with a crime, e.g., the slave killed someone or cut off someone's hand, or occupied with a debt, e.g., he destroyed someone's property for which he is liable, or he became sick, and all these things occurred while he was in the usurper's possession. Similarly, a female slave who was non-pregnant when usurped, but when returned she is pregnant, and this pregnancy occurred in the usurper's possession; this is deficient ada. Similarly, a seller sold a male or female slave; at the time of sale, the sold item was free from defects; when the buyer later took possession, the sold item was defective with one of the mentioned defects; this is also deficient ada. Even if he [the buyer] gets possession by that cause, this is a branch on its being deficient. If this sold item, occupied with a crime, died as a result of that crime, then the possession is invalidated according to Abu Hanifa. So according to Abu Hanifa, this possession becomes void, as if the buyer had not taken possession. Therefore, the buyer will return the full price to the seller. According to them (the Sahibayn), this is a defect, and a defect does not prevent complete delivery and possession. Therefore, the buyer's possession is complete, like the payment of counterfeit (ziyuf) dirhams. For example, a person pays counterfeit dirhams to the creditor for his debt, and the creditor is unaware; this possession is complete. Even if this occupied slave perishes at the buyer's, his right is void; he cannot return the full price, but he can return the deficiency. And similarly, the dispute will be concerning the female slave who became pregnant at the usurper's, then he returned her, and she perished at the owner's due to the same cause: according to the Imam, the usurper is liable for the full value; according to the Sahibayn, there is no liability. And the payment that resembles qada: like when the father of a woman is a slave of a person, then that person marries the woman and appoints her father as the dowry (mahr). Then the woman becomes the owner of her father by the contract itself, and he becomes free due to the rule: 'Whoever owns a mahram relative, he becomes free.' Then this slave (the woman's father) becomes claimed (mustahaqq), i.e., another person claims that he is his slave, and the judge decides in his favor. Then the woman's ownership and emancipation become void, and the husband becomes liable for his value. And if the judge does not decide (neither for the claim nor for the liability of the value on the husband), until he (the husband) becomes the owner of this slave (the woman's father) a second time, then the husband is obliged to hand over this slave to the woman. This delivery is ada in the sense that the slave is the very right of the woman (ayn haqq al-mar'ah) that she is entitled to as the mahr in the marriage contract. So this delivery, in that it is her very right, is ada. Therefore, he cannot prevent her. When the woman demands, 'Hand over this slave who is my father to me,' the husband cannot withhold him from her. This is all from the perspective of its being ada. And from the perspective that the ownership of this slave has changed because it left the owner's possession and came into the husband's possession, and the change of ownership...
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary explains the classification of payment (ada') in the rights of humans (huquq al-ibad). The author first notes that rights of humans are divided into three types of payment: complete (kamil), deficient (qasir), and that resembling qada (shabih al-qada). He then provides examples. Complete ada involves delivering the very same specific item (ayn) that is owed in its original condition. Examples include returning the very item usurped, delivering the sold item as it was at contract, and in currency exchange (sarf) and salam contracts, where the specific counter-value or muslam fihi is treated as the very right owed to avoid prohibited substitution before possession. Deficient ada occurs when the item is delivered with a new defect or encumbrance, such as a slave who commits a crime or becomes pregnant while in the usurper's possession. This leads to a dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that such defects invalidate the possession (qabd) entirely, so the buyer can return the item and get a full refund. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) view the defect as a mere flaw that does not prevent possession; the buyer can only claim a reduction in price. The third type, resembling qada, is illustrated by a case where a woman's father is a slave, the husband marries her and sets the father as mahr, the father becomes free by relative ownership, then a third party successfully claims him, and later the husband reacquires him. In this scenario, the husband must deliver the slave to the wife, which is considered ada because the slave is the very right she is owed as mahr, despite the change in ownership. The text is cut off at the end of this example.

Key Terms
اداء قاصر (ada qasir): Delivery of an item with a new defect or encumbrance
قبض (qabd): Taking possession of an item
انتقاض القبض (intiqad al-qabd): Invalidation of possession; as if it never occurred

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the key difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding a defective item being delivered?
A) Abu Hanifa says the buyer can only claim a reduction; Sahibayn say the buyer can return the item.
B) Abu Hanifa says possession is invalid; Sahibayn say possession is valid.
C) Abu Hanifa says the seller bears all risk; Sahibayn say the buyer bears all risk.
D) Both agree, but differ on the amount of reduction.

Key Takeaway
The effect of defects on possession divides Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, with concrete differences in risk allocation and buyer recourse.
